Implementation Plan — LocateAnything-3B Web Demo

Project location on host filesystem: /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/website/ (a new sibling directory inside the existing locate_anything_setup project).

Reference / sibling project on host filesystem: /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/ — the existing NVIDIA LocateAnything-3B inference container that this new website/ project connects to as a client. This document repeatedly cites file paths and line numbers inside that sibling project; the implementation agent must read those files directly to mirror established conventions.

Host machine context: The implementation runs on the user's personal server running Ubuntu 24.04 LTS, with static LAN IPv4 address 10.0.0.199, exposed to the public IPv4 internet via the residential router's DMZ (Demilitarized Zone) feature. The host machine has both a discrete NVIDIA GeForce RTX 5090 GPU and an integrated Intel iGPU; the discrete GPU is used exclusively by the LocateAnything-3B inference container; the iGPU drives the desktop. See /home/user/Desktop/personal_server/README.md for the host-level setup.

Document date: 2026-06-01. All pinned versions verified live against crates.io and Docker Hub on this date.

This document is the single source of truth. The implementation agent reading this HTML file does not have access to the conversation history that produced it. Every load-bearing decision, every pinned version, every API signature, every byte-level wire-format detail, every cross-component constraint, every verbatim user requirement, and every honest gap is recorded here. If a topic appears underspecified, the implementation agent is empowered (and expected) to spawn its own research sub-agents per Section 5 — Research Methodology.

1. Executive Summary #

This project (./website/) is a publicly-internet-exposed WebRTC Selective Forwarding Unit (SFU) plus single-page WebAssembly frontend that demonstrates the NVIDIA LocateAnything-3B vision-language model over real-time video. It runs entirely inside a single Docker container; nothing is installed on the host operating system.

High-level data flow:

  1. A user (the "streamer") opens the demo Hypertext Transfer Protocol Secure (HTTPS) Uniform Resource Locator (URL) in their web browser, providing a shared-secret authentication token in the URL fragment (the part after the # character).
  2. The web browser downloads a Rust-compiled-to-WebAssembly Single Page Application (SPA) built with the Leptos 0.8.19 framework.
  3. The streamer clicks "Claim Streamer" in the SPA, which sends a WebSocket Secure (WSS) message to the demo server claiming ownership of the single available streaming slot.
  4. If granted, the SPA prompts the user to select a webcam (from any platform: Apple iPhone smartphone, Google Pixel Android smartphone, Samsung Galaxy S25 Android smartphone, Apple iPad tablet, Microsoft Windows laptop, Apple macOS desktop, etc.), and to construct a prompt from the 7 canonical templates LocateAnything-3B was trained on.
  5. The streamer's web browser captures 1280x720-pixel video at 30 frames per second via the JavaScript navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia() Application Programming Interface (API), encodes with H.264 Constrained Baseline Level 3.1, and sends it via WebRTC (Web Real Time Communication) to the demo server, which is a Selective Forwarding Unit.
  6. The demo server has two simultaneous responsibilities for the incoming H.264 video stream: (a) re-publish the Real-time Transport Protocol (RTP) packets to all currently-connected viewer browsers, and (b) sample the latest decoded frame at whatever cadence the LocateAnything-3B inference server can sustain (stop-and-wait per WebSocket: one frame in, one reply out — Section 19.1), decoding H.264 access units to YUV color space, converting to Red-Green-Blue (RGB) color space, encoding as Joint Photographic Experts Group (JPEG) images at quality 92, and sending each JPEG over a WebSocket connection to the inference server.
  7. LocateAnything-3B processes each JPEG and returns a JavaScript Object Notation (JSON) message containing bounding-box coordinates. The demo server normalizes coordinates to the floating-point range [0.0, 1.0] and forwards each BoxMessage over WebRTC Data Channel to the streamer and every viewer in parallel. The video and box flows are architecturally independent: video re-publish (RTP fan-out) does not pass through the decode-pipeline / LA path, and slow LA inference does not slow the live video.
  8. Each browser overlays bounding boxes on a Hypertext Markup Language (HTML) <canvas> element positioned above its <video> element under Strategy A — latest-wins: every canvas redraw tick draws the most-recent BoxMessage received over the Data Channel, on whatever frame is currently being presented. The overlay is therefore stale by one LocateAnything-3B inference cycle plus pipeline overhead (~800 ms hybrid; see Section 21.2 for the honest budget). The streamer's local video has near-zero latency and uses requestAnimationFrame as the redraw cadence (local getUserMedia tracks have no RTP timeline per the WICG video-rvfc spec); the viewer's video uses requestVideoFrameCallback (universal across the Section 22.1 matrix as of 2026-06-02) as the redraw tick so that the canvas redraw matches the actual video-frame presentation cadence even under congestion. The has_rvfc() feature-detect at viewer-mount surfaces a chained anyhow::Error to the error banner if absent (strict no-silent-fallback per Section 3.1).
  9. When the streamer disconnects (closes the browser tab, loses network, or explicitly releases ownership), the demo server's ownership finite state machine reverts cleanly to the Idle state, all viewer WebRTC peer connections are torn down, and the next person to visit the URL can claim the streamer slot.

Critical non-functional properties:

  • Sovereign: No third-party services (no Cloudflare Session Traversal Utilities for Network Address Translation [STUN] server, no Google STUN server, no Let's Encrypt Automated Certificate Management Environment [ACME] client). The demo server runs its own RFC 8489-compliant STUN binding-request handler on the same User Datagram Protocol (UDP) port as the WebRTC media socket.
  • No certificate expiry surprises: A self-signed cert with maximum-validity (824 days, just under Apple Security framework's hard 825-day cap) is generated by the server at first start and persisted in the project-local ./website/.runtime/state/ directory. Operator regenerates approximately every 27 months via ./setup.sh --regenerate-cert (Section 24.7); the wrapper removes the persisted cert files and restarts the service, which detects the missing cert and emits a fresh one.
  • Defensive correctness: No silent fallbacks, no graceful degradation. If anything fails, the server emits a chained-context error string to the client and refuses to proceed. No unwrap(), no expect(), no panic!() in runtime Rust code. All errors are anyhow::Result<T> propagated to the top-level boundary.
  • Default loopback-only: Container binds Transmission Control Protocol port 8443 and User Datagram Protocol port 51000 on IPv4 loopback (127.0.0.1) by default. The --bind-all-interfaces command-line flag flips the binds to 0.0.0.0. IPv4-only, both modes — the user's verbatim requirement names 127.0.0.1 and 0.0.0.0, neither of which is an IPv6 address; the binary does not attempt to dual-stack, the cert does not include an IPv6 SAN, and the smoke test does not probe an IPv6 listener. Browser clients on the loopback reach the demo at https://127.0.0.1:8443 or via a hostname that resolves to an IPv4 address. The operator (user) explicitly gates the --bind-all-interfaces transition with their approval.
  • Operator's home directory, not system-wide: the project lives entirely under the operator's home directory at ~/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/website/ (a subfolder of the existing reference project). All runtime state — TLS cert, private key, the operator's configuration — lives in the gitignored ./website/.runtime/ subdirectory, owned by the operator's user account. No sudo, no /etc/, no /var/. The Docker container runs as the operator's UID/GID via --user "$(id -u):$(id -g)"; files written by the container are owned by the operator on the host.
  • Minimal operator decisions: running the system requires the operator to supply four values exactly once (LocateAnything-3B host + port, an auth secret, and the public hostname browsers reach the demo at) via ./setup.sh --la-host HOST --la-port PORT --auth-secret SECRET --public-host HOST. Everything else is a project-internal constant (image tag, state directory, asset directory, container name, TCP/UDP ports, FSM timeouts, etc.) that the operator never names.
  • Pinned versions everywhere: Every Rust crate, every Docker base image (by Secure Hash Algorithm 256-bit digest), every Advanced Package Tool (APT) package, every WebAssembly build tool. See Section 7.

2. Verbatim User Requirements #

Recorded directly from the user's messages during the planning conversation. These are non-negotiable.

"I want to create a website for demoing locate_anything_setup. But, I only have one instance, one GPU running that website. This computer is exposed to the public internet (public IPv4 address) on whatever port you use to listen on 0.0.0.0. The other computer that's running our locateanything, is not."
"I want you to create a project within /website subfolder of this project that is a web server written in Rust, running entirely within docker (not installing anything on this PC). And a frontend in webassembly (served by the same Rust server that serves the API requests, according to web's one-origin rule)."
"The idea is that the webassembly-based frontend has two way video streaming with the Rust server, and the Rust server samples video frames and passes them to the locateanything algorithm and passes the bounding boxes to the frontend as they're incoming. Obviously, then in the frontend they get overlayed onto whatever video is currently being displayed."
"The way it should work is simple — authentication by having a password embedded within the URL (if that's secure, but tell me if that's not secure enough to expose to the public internet). But it should support multiple users at once as follows — if nothing is yet active, anybody visiting the password-linked https website (all API endpoints of the website protected securely by this password-in-link, BTW) can 'take ownership' and essentially 'begin streaming', then it uses their webcam — whether they're on an Android Phone, iPhone, Windows Laptop, MacOS, iPad, Firefox or Chrome. They should somehow be able to choose which camera to use."
"Ideally use an existing library that already handles all this (a trusted frontend library, tell me if you find no good library for webassembly frontend though). Then once somebody has taken ownership (extremely strict server-side input validation and API endpoint validation, BTW, only allowing one person to take ownership at a time), their webcam begins streaming and they will see the bounding boxes relayed back and overlayed onto their screen, of course in a delay — the overlay detection boxes will come in both a transport delay, and the AI service delay."
"Everybody else who is visiting the password protected website at that moment will also have the video stream from the Rust server, to their devices as well!! And then will also receive the bounding boxes in a delay — this time only the AI processing delay."
"It's extremely important for the inputs to the server to be extremely well validated and strict!!! The server should be very much rigid. If anybody disconnects from the server, the server should correctly clean up the resources, and if the user who took ownership disconnects in any way, the server should cleanly and correctly revert back to a mode where anybody can take ownership."
"This entire server that serves webassembly Rust-based website and also serves API requests via https, should all exist within a docker image, that is programmatically created by the project that you will create at that subfolder of our project, with a required parameter we give the docker image instance launch which is where our server exists (what IP). The whole setup should absolutely survive restart, and be just as correct, reliable and high quality as the locate_anything_setup."
"There shouldn't be options for things, just sovereign, specific, secure but not overengineered secure solutions."
"The default launch should launch the docker image such that the only port we listen on is on 127.0.0.1, then just as with the locate_anything_setup server project, there should be a flag that needs to be set to set up the server in such a way as to listen on 0.0.0.0. You'll only get to expose on 0.0.0.0 after I fully approve the correctness of your implementation."
"Please do well and be defensively correct, and yet specific and not duplicated so that it's easy for me when you eventually do finish and I'll ask you about the implementation. Did I already mention that I care about correctness?"
"The whole flow should be sort of UDP-style. Not actually UDP, but people who truly care about correctness should know when to fire and forget, and when it essentially would actually be unreliable and wrong to 'check if a user is connected'. Sometimes it's none of our business. I hate connections — it makes it so hard to make sure things are correct. But there's no choice, that's how NAT works, NAT only works through TCP, so we have to do extra work to be defensively correct given the fact that we are using connection oriented protocol."
"The sampling from the video should be done at the highest quality, utilizing a bunch of the CPU, I guess using a dedicated library within the docker image or something."
"When we talk about HTTPs, that's for encryption and validity of any encryption and/or API authentication endpoints, but we still need to be sovereign, I don't want the API server to stop working in a year for no reason just because some sort of 'certificate' has expired."
"Only make decisions based on extensive research. You have very capable online research agents at your disposal, and you can tell your agents to clone specific software versions into /tmp for more thorough investigation."
"Pin all versions! Your unlimited sequential research agent budget will be extremely useful for that usecase, so you don't make up versions."
"The router and switch all in one are on a shabbos clock." (Meaning the LAN router that contains both the WAN-side router and the internal LAN switch loses power for 1–3 minutes daily at approximately 05:00 local time, due to a mechanical time-switch device. This is intentional hardware behavior the design must tolerate gracefully.)
"We will also need to research about the host packages that will need to be installed on our docker image, and how."
"There's also much more to research about the webassembly, and the displaying of the video when our frontend is the one providing the video, and the displaying when our frontend is receiving the video live from the server. The details here to get the correctness and performance correct for our specific usecase is pretty crucial."
"When a user takes control, then [they] should get to choose out of the prompts NVIDIA has trained on, and then actually specify the prompt. That's pretty crucial. And it should be very obvious from the UI what the options are, with no room for mistake. Try to place the validation in the frontend only in order not to duplicate. ... The UI should actually be friendly for both mobile and Desktop to allow a user to build the prompt in a way that's like the model has actually been trained on."
"Our Rust web server should also be just as well designed in terms of only one way to do things, and nothing optional or fallback. Instead strict with error handling that actually propagates from within our rust server that is deployed in the docker image."
"The Rust code should be structured as such that the errors propagate in string value. I don't care about like error codes or like programmatic handling of unexpected errors. ... But the error messages should contain the relevant context for debugging the issue. And if it's in the context of a user query, it should be returned as a string to the user propagated correctly as a dynamic string. ... Like the error handling in the Rust code should propagate all the way up. You know, as Bernard Russell said, turtles all the way down. No unwrap, no expect, no panic. OK. And yet, strict correctness, no fallbacks."

Critical user clarifications about Sovereign, third-party-free design:

"How is specifying --public-ip a legitimate thing? We have to remember that we're gonna be exposed to the public internet. ... What the hell are you talking about cloudflare!!! What happened to our personal server that has a public IP!! This very computer."

This means: (a) a separate --public-ip Command-Line Interface (CLI) argument is forbidden because we already have --public-host for the Transport Layer Security (TLS) certificate Subject Alternative Name (SAN); reuse that single configuration knob to drive WebRTC ICE (Interactive Connectivity Establishment) host candidates and the STUN server URL as well. (b) The demo server itself answers STUN binding-request packets from browser clients; we do not delegate this to Cloudflare, Google, Mozilla, or any other third party. Our publicly-routable host is our own STUN server, on User Datagram Protocol port 51000, the same port the Selective Forwarding Unit uses for WebRTC media.

Project scope and pace:

"Implement in full, utilize research agents as needed, we literally have all night so we're not at all anywhere near being in a hurry, the only priority is for high quality and correctness."
"When you use research agents, run them sequentially, because we truly have all day."
"Research is absolutely a cornerstone of correctness, so research as much as possible at every corner of this implementation."

"Your unlimited sequential research agent budget will be extremely useful for that usecase, so you don't make up versions."
"Run each subagent very well instructed, sequentially. And even tell each subagent where to look at in the report. And explain to it things in a well briefed manner. And tell it that it has full capability to clone specific versions of things into /tmp. And perform very extensive research based on that and online research. For documentations and whatever else it needs. Then after each subagent run, perform an edit correction across the report."
"Obviously, the most important thing is to tell the sub-agents where things are, and for you to actually make decisions, not based on what the sub-agents recommend, but based on the knowledge the sub-agents give you and my requirements, and instructions."
"We are allowed to spawn sub-agents that can clone specific versioned stuff that we're using into /tmp for more extensive research. That's non-obvious and super important."

Honesty about shortcuts and gaps:

"Be honest when you're done about any shortcuts you did."
"Don't give me a list of things that you think are already trivial and easy and you already know the answer to. Don't be afraid to list things that might open cans of worms."

Writing style of this plan document (the implementation agent reads this without conversation context):

The implementations of agent will later be given your HTML and will not know anything that you know. So you need to literally explain to it everything that you know, the syntaxes that you have discovered."

"When I say nothing is obvious, I mean call things by their full name. For example, Samsung Galaxy S25 smartphone instead of just Galaxy S25."
"Where things are, that's important."

Source-code path hygiene (what the implementation agent writes into actual files in the project tree):

"It's important to only reference either relative project files, or global versioned resource (including https://github.com/BigBIueWhale/personal_server if needed, I guess that one specifically doesn't have to be versioned though). And yes, global documentations and other versioned resources, within our actual implementation. Meaning, it should be a user-requested requirement in the html report not to reference within the actual eventual written source code any files that are local to our computer like /home/user or /tmp within the actual code implementation or comments."

Operational meaning of this requirement, codified in Section 3.7:

  • Code-level citations to source (Rust // comments, shell # comments, Markdown documentation, etc.) MUST reference either: (a) relative paths within this project's own file tree, (b) a global versioned resource (crate name + version, GitHub URL at a specific tag, RFC number, W3C specification URL), or (c) the user's own https://github.com/BigBIueWhale/personal_server (which is permitted unversioned).
  • Code-level citations MUST NOT reference any local-to-the-host-machine path such as /tmp/..., /home/user/..., /Users/..., or any clone-directory name that exists only on the developer's machine.
  • This applies ONLY to files committed to the project source tree. Prose inside this plan document (which the implementation agent reads but never commits) may freely reference clone directories during research; the plan's own citations are documentation of research, not source code that ships.
  • Practical guidance: prefer "str0m 0.20.0 src/lib.rs:1395" or "https://docs.rs/str0m/0.20.0/src/str0m/lib.rs.html#1395" in a Rust comment over "/tmp/str0m-src/src/lib.rs:1395".

The plan document itself is ephemeral and MUST NOT be referenced from committed source. Verbatim user requirement, added 2026-06-01:

"Code shouldn't mention this report, because eventually this html report won't exist."

Operational meaning, codified in Section 3.8:

  • Committed source files (Rust, shell, Dockerfile, Cargo.toml, etc.) MUST NOT contain references to this plan.html document, to its section numbers (Section 11.7, per Section 17.5), to its Appendix A list, or to any other artifact whose existence ends when the plan is retired.
  • If a code comment needs to encode the WHY of a decision the plan documents, it must state the WHY directly with versioned external citations — not by deferring to "see plan.html Section N.M".
  • The plan document is the working memory of the design process; the committed source is its durable output. Once implementation lands, the plan can be archived or deleted without leaving dangling references in code.
  • The CI lint script in Section 24.10 enforces this for committed files.

3. Defensive Correctness Principles #

These principles override all default behavior. The implementation agent reading this document must understand them deeply.

3.1 No silent fallbacks

If anything fails — a parse, a network operation, a validation check, a precondition — the failure must be surfaced loudly. The system must not invent default values, retry forever without bound, or substitute a degraded behavior. The reference project at /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/ demonstrates this throughout: the Dockerfile fails the entire build on any check failure with set -Eeuo pipefail and explicit test -n "${ARG}" assertions; the Rust server uses #[serde(deny_unknown_fields)] on every wire structure; the flash-attention build for compute capability sm_120 does not fall through to a different attention implementation if the build fails.

3.2 Fail loud, no graceful degradation

A user prefers a clear stop and visible error message to a system that limps along producing wrong answers. This applies at every layer: configuration validation at startup (refuse to start if --auth-secret is shorter than 16 characters); request validation (reject any JSON body with unknown fields); WebSocket message validation (reject any message that does not match the canonical SignalMessage enum variants); prompt validation (reject any prompt that does not match one of the 7 canonical templates from /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/worker/prompts.py); etc.

3.3 Sovereign by default

If we can run a service ourselves, we run it ourselves. The implementation agent must always ask, before considering any third-party dependency: "Can we own this?" Examples already settled by research:

  • STUN server: We run our own RFC 8489-compliant STUN binding-request handler on the same User Datagram Protocol port as our Selective Forwarding Unit. We do not point browser clients at stun:stun.l.google.com:19302 or stun:stun.cloudflare.com:3478.
  • TLS Certificate: Self-signed via the rcgen Rust crate version 0.14.8. We do not use Let's Encrypt (the Automated Certificate Management Environment introduces an external runtime dependency on the Let's Encrypt service and its rate limits).
  • Traversal Using Relays around Network Address Translation (TURN): Deferred. If telemetry shows the ICE failure rate exceeds 2 percent sustained over two consecutive windows of 100 admitted peers, we will run our own coturn TURN server in a sidecar container. We will not use a public TURN service.
  • HyperText Transfer Protocol Strict Transport Security (HSTS): Omitted. HSTS would pin browsers to refuse to bypass certificate warnings after certificate regeneration — exactly the failure mode we are designing against.

3.4 Cross-component constraint tracing

When picking any component or value, the implementation agent must trace constraints across the entire system end-to-end. Example: the capture resolution choice of 1280-by-720 pixels at 30 frames per second is not driven by LocateAnything-3B's preferred input (which would suggest 2560-by-1440 pixels using 75 percent of its 6400-token budget) but by the codec ceiling. The canonical browser-compatible H.264 profile-level identifier across our device matrix is 42e01f (Constrained Baseline Level 3.1); Level 3.1 caps at 1280-by-720 pixels at 30 frames per second. Apple Safari additionally advertises 640c1f (Constrained High) as its preferred entry, so we force 42e01f on both ends via server-side str0m H.264-only config (Section 20.1.1) plus client-side RtcRtpTransceiver::set_codec_preferences() filtering (Section 20.1.2). Going higher than Level 3.1 would mean relying on the optional max-fs and max-mbps Session Description Protocol overrides that browsers MAY interpret — not safe across the device matrix.

3.5 Audit the menu before picking from it

Common failure mode for research agents: choosing between {Cloudflare STUN, Google STUN, Mozilla STUN, etc.} when the actual correct answer is "we run our own". Before picking from any menu of options, the implementation agent must ask whether the menu itself is the right framing. Same with proposing new Command-Line Interface arguments: check whether an existing CLI argument already carries the same information (the --public-host versus --public-ip story).

3.6 Research must exhaust source before flagging gaps

The phrase "worth a smoke check" or "verify with a real build" or "the user should test this" in a research output is a punt, not an honest gap. If a question is answerable by reading cloned source (the create_nonce flag's behavior in trunk build --release; a crate's API signature; test fixtures inside tests/ directories; a method's reachability), the research must read the file. Honest gaps contain only things that genuinely require empirical hardware measurement, undocumented browser quirks, or behavior reserved for future versions.

3.7 No local-machine paths in committed source — versioned citations only

The plan's prose may freely reference clone directories like /tmp/str0m-src/src/lib.rs:1395 because this HTML document is documentation, not source code that ships. But ANY file committed to the project tree (Rust source, shell scripts, Cargo.toml comments, Markdown documentation, Dockerfile, etc.) MUST cite using only:

  • Relative project paths — e.g., ../wasm-client/dist/index.html (from server/build.rs reaching the WASM bundle), ../../../worker/prompts.py (from protocol/src/lib.rs reaching the sibling LocateAnything-3B project's worker/ directory).
  • Versioned crate references — e.g., str0m 0.20.0 src/lib.rs:1395 (anyone can re-fetch via cargo download or https://docs.rs/str0m/0.20.0/src/).
  • GitHub URLs pinned to a tag — e.g., https://github.com/algesten/str0m/blob/0.20.0/src/lib.rs#L1395.
  • RFC and W3C specification numbers / URLs — e.g., RFC 8489 §14.2, https://www.w3.org/TR/webrtc/#dom-rtcrtptransceiver-setcodecpreferences. Cite an external section with the § symbol, never the word "Section" — the Section 24.10 lint reserves the word "Section N.M" for detecting plan references, so RFC 6184 §8.2.2 passes the lint but RFC 6184 Section 8.2.2 is (deliberately) flagged.
  • The user's own https://github.com/BigBIueWhale/personal_server — permitted unversioned (it is the canonical reference for the host's deployment posture).

Local-machine paths that MUST NOT appear in committed source:

  • /tmp/..., /home/user/..., /Users/... (any path that exists only on the developer's machine).
  • Any clone-directory name without a version anchor (str0m-src/, tokio-src/, leptos-src/ — these are research scratch names, not stable references).

The CI lint script in Section 24.10 enforces this for committed files. Plan-prose violations are not enforced (the plan stays as it is, with its rich research-citation history); only files in the eventual source tree are checked.

3.8 No references to this plan document in committed source

The plan document is the working memory of the design process. The committed source — Rust, shell, Dockerfile, configuration files — is its durable output. Once implementation lands, the plan can be archived or deleted without leaving dangling references in code. Therefore, no committed source file may name plan.html, cite "Section N.M" or "Appendix A" of the plan, or otherwise depend on the plan's continued presence to be intelligible.

Forbidden in committed source files:

  • Any literal filename match for plan.html (case-insensitive).
  • // per Section ..., // see Section ..., // (Section N.M), # Section ..., etc. — references to the plan's section numbering.
  • Appendix A, Section 11.8 step 7, or any other plan-internal landmark.
  • Phrases like "the plan says", "documented in the plan", "per the implementation plan", etc.

What committed source SHOULD do instead:

  • If a code comment needs to encode the WHY of a non-obvious decision, state the WHY directly. Cite versioned upstream sources (crate documentation, RFC numbers, W3C URLs, source-line citations to pinned crate versions). The plan's research history is the SOURCE of those citations, not their PROVENANCE.
  • For broad architectural cross-references that don't have a clean upstream citation (e.g., "the FSM transition logic"), name the module or function being cross-referenced: // see also the Sfu::on_disconnect handler in sfu.rs. The reference resolves inside the project tree; it does not depend on the plan.
  • For wire-format and protocol invariants, prefer a doc-comment on the relevant type/function over a free-floating comment.

The CI lint script in Section 24.10 enforces this for committed files. As with Section 3.7, plan-prose self-references (this section pointing to "Section 24.10") are not enforced — only files in the eventual source tree are checked.

4. Rust Error-Handling Style #

Quoted verbatim from the user: "The Rust code should be structured as such that the errors propagate in string value. ... No unwrap, no expect, no panic. ... Yet, strict correctness, no fallbacks."

4.1 Required conventions

  • Every fallible function returns anyhow::Result<T> from the anyhow crate version 1.0.95. No thiserror-style typed error enums. No custom error codes. The error message carries debugging context, not the type.
  • Context layering: Every ?-propagation site that adds useful context gets .context("...") or .with_context(|| format!("...")). Renders via format!("{e:#}") to print the full chain like outer: caused by: middle: caused by: inner.
  • No .unwrap(), no .expect(), no panic!() in runtime code. Hard rule. Tests and benchmarks may use .unwrap() for setup brevity since that code does not ship in the production binary.
  • Turtles all the way down: Errors propagate from the leaf function up through every layer to the top-level boundary (the HTTP handler, the WebSocket handler, or the main supervisor task). Never swallow an error with let _ = ....
  • User-facing errors become Hypertext Transfer Protocol response bodies (the chained error string itself) or WebSocket error messages (JSON {"type":"error","code":"<string-code>","message":"<chained-string>"}) sent to the client before the close frame. The HTTP status code is chosen based on failure class (400 for input validation, 401 for authentication, 429 for rate-limit, 500 for internal), but the body is always the full chained string.
  • Internal logic errors (no user attached, e.g., a background task fails) propagate to the top-level supervisor task in main.rs, which logs via the tracing crate version 0.1.44 and exits or restarts per policy.
  • Strict no-fallback still holds: errors propagate cleanly, but the code does not recover or substitute defaults. Error propagation is not graceful degradation.

4.2 Build script style

The Cargo build scripts (build.rs) use fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> returning errors via the ? operator. Cargo prints the error chain cleanly on build failure. No panic!() even in build.rs.

4.3 Converting from Option and from JsValue

  • Converting Option<T> to anyhow::Result<T>: use .ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!("missing: ...")).
  • Converting JavaScript JsValue errors (which arise in WebAssembly code calling browser APIs through wasm-bindgen) to anyhow::Error: use the js_err helper function. The canonical implementation is in Section 4.5.8 — it downcasts to js_sys::Error first to extract .name() and .message() for browser-API errors, falls back to JsValue::as_string(), and finally to {v:?} Debug. Do not duplicate the body here; use the Section 4.5.8 version.

4.4 Anyhow on the WebAssembly target — REQUIRED, not optional

The anyhow crate's default std feature compiles cleanly on wasm32-unknown-unknown because the standard library is available on the WebAssembly target including std::error::Error. The WebAssembly client uses anyhow::Result<T> for every fallible function, identically to the server. This is a deliberate, single-way decision; the implementation agent does not have a choice between "anyhow" and "raw Result<_, JsValue>" — anyhow is the only path.

The reason is symmetry of discipline: server-side and client-side error chains read the same in logs, in user-facing strings, and in the Leptos RwSignal<Option<String>> error banner. The implementation cannot drift between two styles. Bundle-size cost is estimated under 8 kilobytes after wasm-opt — acceptable.

JavaScript JsValue errors (which arise from browser API calls through wasm-bindgen) are converted to anyhow::Error via the helper in Section 4.3 (js_err); the helper composes with .context(...) the same way as on the server.

4.5 Error wrap-points at every library boundary

Every fallible function returns anyhow::Result<T>; every ?-propagation site that adds useful context calls .with_context(|| format!("...")); errors render via format!("{e:#}") for the full chain. The implementation hits a dozen distinct foreign error types in the source tree. Each one has a specific idiom; below is the verbatim wrap-point recipe per library, with every claim about std::error::Error implementation cited to source at the pinned version.

4.5.1 General rule

anyhow::Result<T>::with_context (and .context) only works if the underlying error type implements std::error::Error + Send + Sync + 'static. The single-line idiom:

some_call().with_context(|| format!("operation X on input Y={y}"))?

becomes, when the source type does NOT implement Error:

some_call().map_err(|e| anyhow::anyhow!("operation X on input Y={y}: {e:?}"))?

The implementation agent uses the first idiom whenever possible because .with_context preserves the source chain via std::error::Error::source(); only the libraries below that lack the Error impl (JsValue, governor::NotUntil) need the explicit anyhow::anyhow! lift.

4.5.2 tokio::task::JoinError (tokio 1.52.3)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl std::error::Error for JoinError {} at tokio-src/tokio/src/runtime/task/error.rs:169. Display renders "task {id} was cancelled" or "task {id} panicked with message {msg:?}" (lines 135-153). No source() because the panic payload is Box<dyn Any + Send>, not a chained Error.

use anyhow::Context;

let handle = tokio::spawn(some_long_running_actor(state.clone()));

let result: anyhow::Result<()> = handle.await
    .with_context(|| format!("join of background task {task_name}"))?  // JoinError -> anyhow::Error
    .with_context(|| format!("inner result of background task {task_name}"))?; // the task's own anyhow::Result

The double ? is intentional: outer extracts the value-or-JoinError, inner extracts the task's own anyhow::Result. If the task panicked, JoinError::Display writes only the panic message string; per Section 4.1's no-panic-in-runtime rule, this is a crash signal, not a recoverable error.

4.5.3 tokio_tungstenite::tungstenite::Error (tungstenite 0.29.0 via tokio-tungstenite 0.29.0)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. #[derive(thiserror::Error, Debug)] at tungstenite-src/src/error.rs:14-76. tokio_tungstenite::tungstenite is a re-export (tokio-tungstenite-0.29.0/src/lib.rs:13: pub use tungstenite;).

Variants worth distinguishing: ConnectionClosed (peer cleanly closed 1000/1001 — NOT semantically an error), AlreadyClosed (programmer bug), Io(io::Error), Tls(TlsError) (never produced for us — LA endpoint is plain ws://), Capacity, Protocol, Utf8, AttackAttempt, Url, Http, HttpFormat.

use anyhow::Context;
use tokio_tungstenite::tungstenite::{Error as WsError, Message};

let reply = ws.next().await
    .ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!("LA WS stream ended mid-frame for frame_id={frame_id}"))?
    .with_context(|| format!("LA WS receive for frame_id={frame_id}"))?;

ws.send(Message::Binary(frame_bytes.into())).await
    .with_context(|| format!("LA WS send of frame_id={frame_id}, jpeg_len={jpeg_len}"))?;

// Reconnect loop MUST match ConnectionClosed as a clean signal, not an error:
loop {
    match ws.next().await {
        Some(Ok(msg))                        => process(msg).await?,
        Some(Err(WsError::ConnectionClosed)) => break Ok(()),  // clean close
        Some(Err(e))                         => return Err(e).context("LA WS recv"),
        None                                 => break Ok(()),  // stream end
    }
}

4.5.4 ffmpeg_next::Error (ffmpeg-next 7.1.0)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl error::Error for Error {} at ffmpeg-next-7.1.0/src/util/error.rs:148. Variants are a flat list of AVERROR codes plus Other { errno } (lines 38-74); Display (lines 156-168) delegates to libavutil's av_strerror.

Gotcha — EAGAIN is NOT an error. libavcodec returns AVERROR(EAGAIN) to mean "I need more input before I can produce output"; this is the canonical encoder/decoder protocol. Match explicitly. Error::Eof similarly means "decoder drained" at end-of-stream.

use anyhow::Context;
use ffmpeg_next::codec::{Context as CodecContext, Id as CodecId};

let mut decoder = CodecContext::new()
    .decoder()
    .open_as(CodecId::H264)
    .context("opening H.264 decoder via libavcodec")?;

decoder.send_packet(&pkt)
    .with_context(|| format!(
        "libavcodec send_packet (NALU bytes={n}, is_keyframe={kf})",
        n = pkt.size(), kf = pkt.is_key()
    ))?;

match decoder.receive_frame(&mut yuv) {
    Ok(()) => {}
    Err(ffmpeg_next::Error::Other { errno }) if errno == ffmpeg_next::error::EAGAIN => {
        return Ok(None);  // need more input; normal
    }
    Err(e) => return Err(e).context("libavcodec receive_frame after H.264 access unit"),
}

4.5.5 mozjpeg 0.10.13 (uses std::io::Error)

Error impl status: N/A — uses std::io::Result<T> directly. Public API returns io::Result from start_compress (mozjpeg-src/src/compress.rs:119), write_scanlines (line 236), finish (line 656). std::io::Error already implements std::error::Error; .with_context(...) works directly.

use anyhow::Context;
use mozjpeg::{ColorSpace, Compress};

let mut c = Compress::new(ColorSpace::JCS_EXT_RGB);
c.set_size(width as usize, height as usize);
c.set_optimize_scans(false);          // disable JCP_MAX_COMPRESSION default — ~45x speedup, baseline JPEG only
c.set_use_scans_in_trellis(false);
c.set_smoothing_factor(0);
c.set_optimize_coding(true);
c.set_quality(92.0);

let mut started = c.start_compress(Vec::new())
    .with_context(|| format!("mozjpeg start_compress (size={w}x{h})", w=width, h=height))?;

started.write_scanlines(&rgb_bytes)
    .with_context(|| format!(
        "mozjpeg write_scanlines (rgb_bytes_len={n}, expected={e})",
        n = rgb_bytes.len(), e = (width as usize) * (height as usize) * 3
    ))?;

let jpeg_bytes: Vec<u8> = started.finish()
    .with_context(|| format!("mozjpeg finish (size={w}x{h}, quality=92)", w=width, h=height))?;

Gotcha — mozjpeg's "may panic" docstring (compress.rs:116-118, 144-146): the upstream libjpeg C library's setjmp/longjmp-based error system wraps as a Rust panic. In our pipeline, malformed input cannot reach mozjpeg (RGB buffer comes from libswscale with guaranteed valid layout). Do NOT wrap in catch_unwind; if a panic occurs, --restart unless-stopped recovers.

4.5.6 str0m::RtcError (str0m 0.20.0)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl Error for RtcError at str0m-src/src/error.rs:125-139, with source() for eight wrapped sub-errors.

Full variant list (str0m-src/src/error.rs:17-87): RemoteSdp(String), Sdp(SdpError), Rtp(RtpError), Io(io::Error), Dtls(DtlsError), Packet(Mid, Pt, PacketError), UnknownPt(Pt), UnknownRid(Rid), NoSenderSource, ResendRequiresRtxPt, NotSendingDirection(Direction), NotReceivingDirection, NoReceiverSource(Option<Rid>), FeedbackNotEnabled(KeyframeRequestKind), Net(NetError), Ice(IceError), Sctp(SctpError), ChangesOutOfOrder, WriteWithoutPoll.

use anyhow::Context;
use str0m::{Output};
use str0m::Input;

// UDP receive branch:
client.rtc.handle_input(input)
    .with_context(|| format!(
        "str0m::Rtc::handle_input for client_id={cid}, src={src}, len={len}",
        cid = client.id, src = src, len = pkt.len()
    ))?;

// poll_output drain loop:
loop {
    match client.rtc.poll_output()
        .with_context(|| format!("str0m::Rtc::poll_output for client_id={cid}", cid = client.id))?
    {
        Output::Timeout(t)   => { client.timeout = Some(t); break; }
        Output::Transmit(tx) => self.udp.send_to(&tx.contents, tx.destination).await
                                    .with_context(|| format!(
                                        "udp send_to {dst} ({len} bytes) for client_id={cid}",
                                        dst = tx.destination, len = tx.contents.len(), cid = client.id
                                    ))?,
        Output::Event(ev)    => self.handle_event(client.id, ev).await?,
    }
}

Per Section 11.7's disconnect-on-Err policy: any RtcError from handle_input or poll_output is terminal for that one client. Do NOT retry handle_input after an error — str0m's state machine becomes inconsistent.

4.5.7 serde_json::Error (serde_json 1.0.150)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl Error for serde_json::Error per docs.rs; Display reports parse position with line() and column().

use anyhow::Context;
use protocol::SignalMessage;

let msg: SignalMessage = serde_json::from_str(&text)
    .with_context(|| format!(
        "parse SignalMessage from inbound WS text (len={len}, first 128 bytes: {head:?})",
        len = text.len(), head = text.as_bytes().get(..text.len().min(128))
    ))?;

let body = serde_json::to_string(&reply)
    .context("serialize SignalMessage reply (structurally impossible — bug if seen)")?;

With #[serde(deny_unknown_fields)], from_str rejects extra fields and returns a useful chained string like "unknown field `foo`, expected one of `bar`, `baz`". Do NOT strip or rewrite it before sending to the client.

4.5.8 JsValue → anyhow::Error on the WebAssembly target

Error impl status: NO Error IMPL. wasm_bindgen::JsValue is a Rust-side handle to an opaque JS object; verified by reading wasm-bindgen 0.2.122 docs.rs trait list. Explicit lift via the js_err helper, improved with js_sys::Error downcast for browser-API errors:

use anyhow::Context;
use wasm_bindgen::{JsCast, JsValue};
use js_sys::Error as JsError;

/// Convert a `JsValue` produced by a failing browser API call into an
/// `anyhow::Error` carrying a human-readable string. Order of attempts:
/// (1) downcast to js_sys::Error and read .message();
/// (2) `JsValue::as_string()` for plain string values;
/// (3) the `{v:?}` Debug fallback (always succeeds).
pub fn js_err(label: &'static str) -> impl FnOnce(JsValue) -> anyhow::Error {
    move |v| {
        let detail: String = v.dyn_ref::<JsError>()
            .map(|e| {
                let name: String = e.name().into();
                let msg:  String = e.message().into();
                format!("{name}: {msg}")
            })
            .or_else(|| v.as_string())
            .unwrap_or_else(|| format!("{v:?}"));
        anyhow::anyhow!("{label}: {detail}")
    }
}

// Usage:
let pc = web_sys::RtcPeerConnection::new_with_configuration(&cfg)
    .map_err(js_err("RtcPeerConnection::new"))
    .context("opening WebRTC peer connection")?;

let offer = wasm_bindgen_futures::JsFuture::from(pc.create_offer())
    .await
    .map_err(js_err("RtcPeerConnection::createOffer"))
    .context("creating SDP offer")?;

4.5.9 rcgen::Error (rcgen 0.14.8)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl std::error::Error for Error {} at rcgen-src/rcgen/src/error.rs:109. The enum is #[non_exhaustive] (line 4); use _ => in any match.

use anyhow::Context;
use rcgen::{CertificateParams, KeyPair, PKCS_ECDSA_P256_SHA256};

let mut params = CertificateParams::new(vec![])
    .context("rcgen CertificateParams::new (empty SAN vec, will populate below)")?;
// ... set params ...

let key_pair = KeyPair::generate_for(&PKCS_ECDSA_P256_SHA256)
    .context("rcgen KeyPair::generate_for(ECDSA_P256_SHA256) via aws-lc-rs")?;

    .context("rcgen self_signed cert issuance")?;

4.5.10 rustls::Error (rustls 0.23.40)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl std::error::Error for Error {} at rustls-src/rustls/src/error.rs:1022.

use anyhow::Context;
use std::{fs::File, io::BufReader};
use rustls::ServerConfig;
use rustls_pemfile::{certs, pkcs8_private_keys};

let cert_chain = certs(&mut BufReader::new(File::open(&cert_path)
        .with_context(|| format!("open cert at {p}", p = cert_path.display()))?))
    .collect::<Result<Vec<_>, _>>()
    .with_context(|| format!("parse PEM cert chain in {p}", p = cert_path.display()))?;

let key = pkcs8_private_keys(&mut BufReader::new(File::open(&key_path)
        .with_context(|| format!("open key at {p}", p = key_path.display()))?))
    .next()
    .ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!("no PKCS8 private key in {p}", p = key_path.display()))?
    .with_context(|| format!("parse PKCS8 private key in {p}", p = key_path.display()))?;

let server_config = ServerConfig::builder_with_protocol_versions(&[&rustls::version::TLS13])
    .with_no_client_auth()
    .with_single_cert(cert_chain, key.into())
    .context("rustls ServerConfig::with_single_cert (TLS 1.3 only, no client auth)")?;

4.5.11 x509_parser::error::X509Error (x509-parser 0.18.1)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. #[derive(thiserror::Error)] at x509-parser-0.18.1/src/error.rs:17; PEMError at line 110 same derive.

Gotcha — nom::Err wrapping. parse_x509_pem and X509Certificate::from_der return nom::Err<X509Error>, not X509Error directly. nom::Err does not implement std::error::Error, so explicit map_err is required.

use anyhow::Context;
use x509_parser::prelude::*;
use x509_parser::pem::parse_x509_pem;

let pem_bytes = std::fs::read(&cert_path)
    .with_context(|| format!("read cert PEM from {p}", p = cert_path.display()))?;

let (_, pem) = parse_x509_pem(&pem_bytes)
    .map_err(|e| anyhow::anyhow!("parse_x509_pem from {p}: {e}", p = cert_path.display()))?;

let (_, cert) = X509Certificate::from_der(&pem.contents)
    .map_err(|e| anyhow::anyhow!("X509Certificate::from_der from {p}: {e}", p = cert_path.display()))?;

let not_after = cert.validity().not_after;
let sans: Vec<String> = cert
    .subject_alternative_name()
    .context("read SubjectAlternativeName extension")?
    .map(|ext| ext.value.general_names.iter().map(|n| format!("{n}")).collect())
    .unwrap_or_default();

4.5.12 tokio::time::error::Elapsed (tokio 1.52.3)

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl std::error::Error for Elapsed {} at tokio-src/tokio/src/time/error.rs:117.

use anyhow::Context;
use std::time::Duration;
use tokio::time::timeout;

match timeout(Duration::from_secs(8), serve_handle).await {
    Ok(Ok(()))   => {}
    Ok(Err(e))   => return Err(e).context("axum serve returned an error during shutdown"),
    Err(elapsed) => return Err(elapsed)
        .context("graceful shutdown exceeded 8 s budget — forcing exit; \
                  per-connection tasks have been notified and will drain themselves"),
}

4.5.13 clap::Error (clap 4.6.1) — let it own the exit

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl<F: ErrorFormatter> error::Error for Error<F> at clap-src/clap_builder/src/error/mod.rs:836. But the canonical pattern is Parser::parse(), which calls .exit() internally on parse error (error/mod.rs:245-249): writes formatted error to stderr and std::process::exit(2) (or 0 for --help/--version). This is intentional and the pattern the clap maintainers recommend.

use clap::Parser;
use anyhow::Context;

#[derive(clap::Parser, Debug)]
#[command(name = "la_website_server", version, about)]
struct Args {
    #[arg(long, value_name = "HOST")]   la_host: String,
    #[arg(long, value_name = "PORT")]   la_port: u16,
    #[arg(long, value_name = "SECRET")] auth_secret: String,
    // ... plus --public-host and the opt-in --bind-all-interfaces flag.
}

#[tokio::main(flavor = "multi_thread", worker_threads = 4)]
async fn main() -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    let args = Args::parse();  // clap auto-renders + exits on parse failure

    if args.auth_secret.len() < 16 {
        anyhow::bail!(
            "--auth-secret too short ({n} chars); must be at least 16 characters",
            n = args.auth_secret.len()
        );
    }

    run(args).await.context("la_website_server main loop")
}

Do NOT wrap clap errors in anyhow. Clap's user-facing rendering ("error: the following required arguments were not provided: …") is exactly what we want; piping through .with_context(...) would prepend an opaque label. The discipline "every fallible function returns anyhow::Result<T>" still holds — parse() succeeds-or-exits, so it is effectively infallible from main's POV.

4.5.14 governor::NotUntil (governor 0.10.4)

Error impl status: NO Error IMPL. NotUntil at governor-src/governor/src/gcra.rs:17 is a status object, not an error. impl<P> fmt::Display for NotUntil<P> (line 71) renders "rate-limited until {time}", but no Error impl. Explicit anyhow::anyhow! lift:

use governor::{RateLimiter, clock::DefaultClock};

fn admit_or_429(limiter: &PerIpLimiter, ip: std::net::IpAddr) -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    match limiter.check_key(&ip) {
        Ok(()) => Ok(()),
        Err(not_until) => {
            let wait = not_until.wait_time_from(DefaultClock::default().now());
            Err(anyhow::anyhow!(
                "rate limit exceeded for {ip}; retry after {wait_ms} ms",
                ip = ip, wait_ms = wait.as_millis()
            ))
        }
    }
}

4.5.15 rustls_pemfile (rustls-pemfile 2.2.0)

Every public function returns Result<…, std::io::Error> (e.g., certs at rustls-pemfile-src/src/lib.rs:85-93; pkcs8_private_keys at line 174). io::Error implements std::error::Error; .with_context(...) works directly (see Section 4.5.10 examples).

4.5.16 aws_lc_rs::error::Unspecified and KeyRejected

Error impl status: VERIFIED. impl Error for KeyRejected at aws-lc-rs-src/aws-lc-rs/src/error.rs:157; impl Error for Unspecified at line 167. Unspecified's deliberate design (lines 14-22): "no detail because side-channels" — the chained string is unavoidably opaque on this path. This is the documented upstream choice. We reach aws-lc-rs only transitively through rcgen and rustls, so direct wrap-points are rare; if needed:

use anyhow::Context;
use aws_lc_rs::rand::{SecureRandom, SystemRandom};

let rng = SystemRandom::new();
let mut buf = [0u8; 32];
rng.fill(&mut buf)
    .map_err(|_| anyhow::anyhow!("aws_lc_rs::SystemRandom::fill failed"))?;

4.5.17 axum::Error (axum 0.8.9 WebSocket extract)

axum::extract::ws::WebSocket::send/recv returns axum::Error, which wraps tokio_tungstenite::tungstenite::Error. axum::Error implements std::error::Error per docs.rs.

use anyhow::Context;
use axum::extract::ws::{Message, WebSocket};

socket.send(Message::Text(payload)).await
    .with_context(|| format!("axum WS send to client_id={cid}, kind={k}", cid=cid, k=kind))?;

let frame = match socket.recv().await {
    Some(Ok(f))  => f,
    Some(Err(e)) => return Err(e).context("axum WS recv"),
    None         => return Err(anyhow::anyhow!("axum WS closed by peer")),
};

5. Research Methodology — Sub-Agents and Source Cloning #

This section is critical and non-obvious. The implementation agent reading this document is empowered to spawn its own research sub-agents at any time during implementation. The user explicitly granted this capability with the quote: "You have very capable online research agents at your disposal, and you can tell your agents to clone specific software versions into /tmp for more thorough investigation." This is how the entire research foundation of this plan was built.

5.1 How to spawn a research sub-agent

The implementation agent has access to the Agent tool. To spawn a research sub-agent, invoke it with subagent_type: "general-purpose" and a detailed prompt. The sub-agent has access to: Bash (to run git clone, curl, find, jq, etc.), Read (to read files), WebFetch (to fetch remote pages), and WebSearch (to query search engines). The sub-agent does not have access to write files in the project tree (or it should not write to the project tree — restrict its work to /tmp for source cloning, and have it return findings as text).

5.2 What the sub-agent should do

For any question that cannot be answered with certainty from this plan document, the implementation agent should:

  1. Clone the relevant pinned-version source code into /tmp. Example: git clone --depth 1 --branch 0.20.0 https://github.com/algesten/str0m.git /tmp/research-str0m.
  2. Verify the current latest stable version of any crate via the crates.io Hypertext Transfer Protocol Application Programming Interface: curl -s https://crates.io/api/v1/crates/<crate-name> | jq -r '.crate.max_stable_version'. The implementation agent should not rely on training-data version numbers.
  3. Read the actual file at the actual line and cite as file:line in the resulting work. Example citation that came out of research: "/tmp/str0m-src/src/lib.rs:1267-1272 — Rtc::disconnect does only self.alive = false; no Real-time Transport Control Protocol Bye message is sent; no Datagram Transport Layer Security close_notify is sent."
  4. Verify across cross-component constraints (codec profile-level versus capture resolution versus inference token budget versus bandwidth ceiling versus device hardware-encoder capability, all simultaneously, not one at a time).
  5. Reject the "honest gap" punt: if a question can be answered by reading source, the sub-agent must read the source. Only genuinely empirical questions (hardware-specific encode latency on the target box; undocumented browser version-specific quirks; new feature behavior not yet in any published release notes) belong in the "honest gaps" section of the output.

5.3 What the sub-agent should not do

  • Do not pick from a menu of third-party services. The answer is almost always "we run our own". See Section 3.5.
  • Do not write files in the project tree (/home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/website/). Limit file writes to /tmp. Implementation belongs to the implementation agent, not the research sub-agent.
  • Do not propose new Command-Line Interface arguments without checking whether an existing one carries the same information. Configuration-surface duplication is a smell.

5.4 Examples of research sub-agent prompts that worked

To brief a sub-agent for source-level verification:

"Today is 2026-06-01. You're doing DEEP, source-level research. You have full
file system access. Clone repos, read source, cite file:line. **No 'consider X'
or 'verify Y empirically' punts.** If a question is answerable from cloned
source, read the source. 'Honest gaps' should contain ONLY things genuinely
unknowable from public source.

## Non-negotiable framing
Sovereign Rust+WebAssembly web service, single shared-secret authentication
token in URL fragment, ECDSA Prime 256-bit elliptic-curve self-signed
certificate with 824-day validity, str0m 0.20.0, axum 0.8.9, ffmpeg-next
7.1.0, mozjpeg 0.10.13. No third-party STUN.

## Required source-cloning at task start
Use Bash:
    git clone --depth 1 --branch 0.20.0 https://github.com/algesten/str0m.git /tmp/str0m-src
    curl -s https://crates.io/api/v1/crates/SOMETHING | jq -r '.crate.max_stable_version'

## Questions you MUST answer definitively (no smoke-check punts)
[specific questions with explicit must-answer rule]

## Methodology
- Clone source. Cite file:line. Under N words. No punts."

5.5 Patterns that surfaced load-bearing facts

Examples of facts surfaced via this methodology that the implementation agent might otherwise have missed:

  • The str0m example file examples/chat.rs calls request_keyframe(... KeyframeRequestKind::Fir) at line 444, but this is wrong per RFC 5104: Full Intra Request (FIR) is reserved for mixer/composition scenarios; Picture Loss Indication (PLI) is the correct modern keyframe-request mechanism. The implementation agent must use KeyframeRequestKind::Pli everywhere, despite str0m's example using Fir.
  • mozjpeg::Compress::new() defaults to the JCP_MAX_COMPRESSION profile (per mozjpeg-rust-src/src/compress.rs:99-103 and the underlying C library mozjpeg-research/jcparam.c:498-500), which silently enables progressive JPEG, multipass optimize_scans search, and trellis quantization. This is the approximately-45-times-slower-than-libjpeg-turbo encoding path. The implementation agent must explicitly call set_optimize_scans(false) to fall back to baseline JPEG encoding.
  • The Apple Security framework (used by Apple Safari on Apple iOS, Apple iPadOS, and Apple macOS, and by Google Chrome and Mozilla Firefox on Apple iOS and Apple iPadOS via WebKit-based shells) enforces an absolute 825-day maximum cert validity period for all Transport Layer Security certificates issued on or after 2020-09-01, including user-trusted self-signed certificates. There is no user-interface bypass. Empirically verified by Michal Špaček: 825-day certificate works, 826-day certificate is rejected with trustd error "Non-system-trusted leaf validity period longer than 825 days and issued on or after 1 July 2019".
  • The Leptos crate version 0.8.18 never existed on crates.io. Verified live 2026-06-01 via curl https://crates.io/api/v1/crates/leptos/0.8.18 returning {"errors":[{"detail":"crate 'leptos' does not have a version '0.8.18'"}]}. The 0.8.x list jumps from 0.8.17 (2026-03-01) directly to 0.8.19 (2026-04-16). Earlier drafts of this plan had the assertion inverted ("0.8.19 does not exist; use 0.8.18") — that was a propagated mistake. Use =0.8.19.
  • The requestVideoFrameCallback Hypertext Markup Language Video Element method is not bound in web-sys crate version 0.3.99 (verified by reading wasm-bindgen-0.2.122/crates/web-sys/src/features/gen_HtmlVideoElement.rs). The implementation agent must hand-write a #[wasm_bindgen(extends = HtmlVideoElement)] extern declaration in the WebAssembly client crate to access this Application Programming Interface, which is needed for per-frame bounding-box overlay synchronization. As of 2026-06-02, every browser in the Section 22.1 matrix implements rVFC — Mozilla Firefox shipped it to release in Firefox 132 (Bugzilla 1919367, released 2024-10-29) and to Firefox for Android in 150 — so the runtime has_rvfc() feature-detection (Section 21.3) is the universal entry point, with no per-browser branching.
  • The str0m Internet Connectivity Establishment consent-freshness timeout is approximately 21.5 seconds, not RFC 7675's nominal 30 seconds. Math: max_retransmits=9; cumulative backoff per str0m-src/crates/is/src/stun.rs:23-28 sums stun_resend_delay(n) for n in 2..=9 (the n=1 step at 250ms is omitted; the algorithm starts at the second retry): 500+1000+2000+3000+3000+3000+3000+3000 = 18500 ms, plus a final 3000-ms wait at the cap = 21500 ms. The library author's comment in source: "libwebrtc uses 8000 here but we want faster detection of gone peers".
  • The str0m 0.20 library has no IceConnectionState::Failed variant in the public enumeration. The variant is commented out in str0m-src/crates/is/src/agent.rs:212 with the comment "the failed and closed state doesn't really have a mapping in this implementation. We never end trickle ICE and it's always possible to come back if more remote candidates are added". The implementation agent watches IceConnectionState::Disconnected events instead.
  • The Debian Trixie (Debian version 13) operating system ships FFmpeg version 7.1.4 with libavcodec61 shared object name (Application Binary Interface). The ffmpeg-next Rust crate version 8.1.0 requires FFmpeg version 8 headers. The implementation must use ffmpeg-next version 7.1.0 instead (released September 2024). Alternatives — mixing Debian Sid Application Package Tool sources into Trixie, or using Debian Sid for the entire base — were rejected as brittle. Ubuntu 26.04 LTS as the base was rejected as too new (6 weeks old as of 2026-06-01).

6. Architecture Overview — Data Flow and Components #

6.1 Component diagram (textual)

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                          Streamer Browser (one)                          │
│  ┌─────────────────┐  ┌────────────────────────┐  ┌────────────────────┐ │
│  │ getUserMedia →  │  │ RTCPeerConnection →    │  │ DataChannel "boxes"│ │
│  │ <video> (local) │  │ H.264 over WebRTC      │  │ ← receives boxes   │ │
│  │ canvas overlay  │  │ media plane (UDP/SRTP) │  │ (JSON, unordered,  │ │
│  │                 │  │                        │  │  unreliable)       │ │
│  └─────────────────┘  └────────────────────────┘  └────────────────────┘ │
│  WebSocket Secure /v1/signal — SDP offer/answer, ICE candidates,         │
│  claim_streamer with {prompt, generation_mode}, keepalive, resume_session│
└──────┬───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
       │ HTTPS+WSS port 8443 (TCP)
       │ WebRTC media+DataChannel port 51000 (UDP)
       ▼
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│              Demo Server Docker Container (this project)                 │
│  Public IPv4: same as host (via DMZ); --network host                     │
│                                                                          │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ axum 0.8.9 HTTPS listener on 8443 (TCP)                            │  │
│  │ ├── /            → static SPA from /var/dist/, no auth             │  │
│  │ ├── /index-*.js  → fingerprinted assets, no auth                   │  │
│  │ ├── /v1/health   → GET, no auth (boolean health bits only)         │  │
│  │ ├── /v1/info     → GET, auth required (container time, cert SANs, git SHA) │
│  │ ├── /v1/capabilities → GET, auth required (prompt template list)   │  │
│  │ └── /v1/signal   → WSS upgrade with auth + rate-limit              │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ SFU actor task (tokio task)                                        │  │
│  │ ├── Single UDP socket on 51000                                     │  │
│  │ ├── str0m 0.20.0 — owns Vec<Client>                                │  │
│  │ ├── Hand-rolled RFC 8489 STUN binding-request handler (~120 LoC)   │  │
│  │ │     demuxed from same UDP socket: DatagramRecv::try_from first;  │  │
│  │ │     on Err, attempt as pre-session STUN; reply with              │  │
│  │ │     XOR-MAPPED-ADDRESS attribute                                 │  │
│  │ ├── Ownership FSM: Idle → Claimed → Streaming → Draining → Idle    │  │
│  │ ├── For incoming H.264 NAL Unit (Network Abstraction Layer Unit)   │  │
│  │ │     access units from streamer's MediaData:                      │  │
│  │ │       (a) republish RTP to every viewer's StreamTx               │  │
│  │ │       (b) push the AU into a bounded mpsc::channel(256) toward   │  │
│  │ │           the decode-pipeline thread; in-order delivery, NO      │  │
│  │ │           coalescing — the H.264 reference chain across          │  │
│  │ │           P-frames is preserved end-to-end.                      │  │
│  │ └── PLI (Picture Loss Indication) keyframe requests, event-driven  │  │
│  │       only — NO periodic scheduler, NO hardcoded interval:         │  │
│  │       (i) proactive on new-viewer attach (~1 RTT saved on the      │  │
│  │       viewer's first-frame); (ii) on MediaData.contiguous=false    │  │
│  │       from the decode thread on packet-loss recovery (str0m chat.rs│  │
│  │       reference pattern). Wire-rate is structurally bounded by     │  │
│  │       str0m's per-50-ms TWCC pass coalescing the pending_request_  │  │
│  │       keyframe field AND by libwebrtc's kMinKeyframeSendInterval   │  │
│  │       Ms=300 encoder-side floor; no application-level throttle    │  │
│  │       is needed on top of those two structural caps.               │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ Decode pipeline (DEDICATED OS thread — scaler is !Send)            │  │
│  │ Drains AUs in arrival order from the bounded mpsc::channel(256).   │  │
│  │ Holds ONE long-lived ffmpeg-next 7.1.0 H.264 decoder Context for   │  │
│  │ the entire streaming session; libavcodec maintains the H.264       │  │
│  │ reference chain across P-frames. Output is held until recovered    │  │
│  │ (libavcodec/h264_slice.c:1376-1383 — no AV_CODEC_FLAG_OUTPUT_      │  │
│  │ CORRUPT means corrupt frames are NEVER emitted by default), so     │  │
│  │ cold-start before the first IDR is naturally silent.               │  │
│  │ On MediaData.contiguous=false: decoder.flush() + emit one          │  │
│  │ event-driven KeyframeRequestKind::Pli upstream.                    │  │
│  │ → YUV420P frame                                                    │  │
│  │ → ffmpeg-next libswscale Pixel::YUV420P → Pixel::RGB24,            │  │
│  │   Flags::BICUBIC, BT.709 colorspace via sws_setColorspaceDetails   │  │
│  │   (limited→full range; matches modern-webcam VUI signaling).       │  │
│  │   Scaling Context is long-lived; reconstructed only on a frame-    │  │
│  │   dimensions change (libavcodec auto-reinit at h264_slice.c:1080). │  │
│  │ → publish RGB frame to tokio::sync::watch::Sender<Option<RgbFrame> │  │
│  │   (1-slot, latest-wins; coalescing is SAFE here because each RGB   │  │
│  │   frame is self-contained — no cross-frame state)                  │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
│  ┌────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐  │
│  │ LA WebSocket client task (tokio task) — the natural-rate driver    │  │
│  │ tokio-tungstenite 0.29.0, default features (TLS not on by default) │  │
│  │ ws://<la-host>:<la-port>/v1/stream                                 │  │
│  │ Wire frame: [4-byte BE u32 = header_len][header_len JSON][JPEG]    │  │
│  │ JSON: {frame_id, prompt, generation_mode, jpeg_len}                │  │
│  │ Loop:                                                              │  │
│  │   jpeg_rx.changed().await    // park if no new frame from decoder  │  │
│  │   frame = jpeg_rx.borrow_and_update().clone()   // latest wins     │  │
│  │   jpeg = mozjpeg encode at quality 92 (set_optimize_scans(false),  │  │
│  │     set_use_scans_in_trellis(false), set_smoothing_factor(0),      │  │
│  │     set_optimize_coding(true), chroma 4:2:0 default)               │  │
│  │   ws.send(wire) ; reply = ws.next().await                          │  │
│  │   forward reply to FSM (LaBoxResult / LaErrorResult)               │  │
│  │ Stop-and-wait per connection (LA enforces). LA's natural latency   │  │
│  │ (~785 ms hybrid, ~937 ms slow per DRONE_DETECTION.md:113-117) is   │  │
│  │ the sampling cadence — no scheduler, no hardcoded interval.        │  │
│  │ Reconnect on close: exponential backoff 500ms..10s.                │  │
│  │ Replies received: forward to FSM, then DataChannel-fanout to peers │  │
│  └────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘  │
└─────────────┬────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘
              │ ws:// on the LAN (10.0.0.x)
              │ no TLS (private network)
              ▼
┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│      LocateAnything-3B Inference Container (existing sibling project)    │
│      Path: /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/                     │
│      Default address: 127.0.0.1:8765 on the LA host; reachable on the    │
│      LAN as <la-host-ip>:8765 only when the LA container is started      │
│      with the --bind-all-interfaces flag (existing flag of that project, │
│      added in commit 3046e58 of locate_anything_setup).                  │
└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Concurrently:

┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│                        Viewer Browsers (zero to N)                       │
│  ┌─────────────────────┐  ┌─────────────────────┐                        │
│  │ <video> ← RTCPeer-  │  │ DataChannel "boxes" │                        │
│  │ Connection from     │  │ ← receives boxes    │                        │
│  │ demo server (SFU)   │  │ (JSON, unordered,   │                        │
│  │                     │  │  unreliable)        │                        │
