/* INSET focus ring (negative offset): drawn inside the border box, so it is
   immune to clipping by any `overflow: clip` ancestor and by the overflow-y:auto
   scroll regions — a focused control flush to a scrollport edge would otherwise
   have an OUTSIDE ring cropped (an ancestor's overflow clips a descendant's
   outline; CSS2 §11.1.1). overflow-clip-margin cannot help here (no effect on
   auto/scroll; unsupported in Safari). Use this inset convention for EVERY
   focusable element — buttons, the prompt cards, and the form inputs added at
   implementation time — not just buttons. */
button:focus-visible  { outline: 2px solid var(--accent); outline-offset: -2px; }
/* On the accent-filled primary button an --accent ring would blend into the
   fill; reuse the #fff the primary button already uses for its label so the
   inset ring stays visible. */
button.primary:focus-visible { outline-color: #fff; }
@media (any-hover: hover) {
    button:hover:not(:disabled) { filter: brightness(1.08); }
}

The full per-component rules (prompt-card, conn-pill, error-banner, preview-pane) are appended to this skeleton at implementation time. Sections 21.1 through 21.13 below describe component-level Leptos shapes and behavior; their layout containers reference the classes defined above.

21.1 Top-level structure

Standard Leptos 0.8.19 Client-Side Rendering application:

// wasm-client/src/lib.rs
use leptos::prelude::*;

fn main() {
    console_error_panic_hook::set_once();
    leptos::mount::mount_to_body(|| view! { <App/> });
}

#[component]
fn App() -> impl IntoView {
    // Read the auth token from window.location.hash on mount.
    let auth_token = auth::read_hash_token();
    let conn_state = RwSignal::new(ConnState::Disconnected);
    let last_error = RwSignal::new(Option::<String>::None);
    // ...
    view! {
        <ErrorBanner error=last_error />
        <ConnectionState state=conn_state />
        // ...
    }
}

21.2 Two display paths — independent latency goals

Video and bounding-box overlays travel on two independent paths with different latency goals:

  • Video path (streamer → SFU → viewer): low-latency live stream. WebRTC over UDP/SRTP, with the SFU re-publishing RTP packets verbatim (no decode, no re-encode). End-to-end target: 120–300 ms typical streamer-camera-to-viewer-screen. This is dramatically lower than YouTube Live (~3–10 s buffer).
  • Boxes path (streamer → SFU → LocateAnything-3B → SFU → ALL peers via DataChannel): one full inference cycle of unavoidable latency, dominated by the upstream model. Boxes go to the streamer AND to every viewer in parallel, so the streamer's box latency is not penalized by viewer fan-out.

Because these are independent paths, slow LA inference does NOT slow the live video stream, and fast video does NOT speed up the boxes. The user's stated goals — "video to viewers ASAP without stutter, boxes for the streamer ASAP" — are met by keeping the two flows architecturally separate, which they already are.

The user has explicitly granted that boxes do NOT need to be displayed on the exact video frame they were inferred from: "no need for the bounding boxes to come in at the same time as the frame being presented." The plan honors this with Strategy A — latest-wins overlay: every browser (streamer and viewer alike) draws the most recent BoxMessage on whatever frame is currently being presented. The box always represents a scene ~one inference cycle in the past relative to the live video on screen; this is irreducible (physics) and consistent with the user's framing.

Streamer path
The user's own browser captures via getUserMedia; the resulting MediaStream is assigned to a local <video> element via HtmlMediaElement::set_src_object. Display latency is essentially zero (browser-internal pipeline). The bounding-box overlay is drawn via requestAnimationFrame (NOT rVFC — rVFC's metadata.rtpTimestamp is absent for local getUserMedia tracks per WICG video-rvfc spec, since local sources have no RTP timeline). On each RAF tick the canvas reads latest_box via RwSignal::with_untracked (no Leptos reactive subscription — pure pull) and renders the most-recent BoxMessage's rectangles. Color: desaturated red #dd5050. A small corner badge displays the running median overlay staleness (computed as below), so the streamer knows roughly how far behind live the overlay is. The staleness is the LA cycle plus pipeline overhead — ~785 ms hybrid, ~937 ms slow, ~210 ms point_to as of LA-3B (per /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/docs/DRONE_DETECTION.md:113-117); a model swap changes this one-for-one without architectural change.

Staleness-badge construction (buildable, no getStats). The badge answers "how far behind live is my overlay?" — which, under Strategy A plus LocateAnything-3B's stop-and-wait pipeline, is essentially one inference cycle. Measure it directly and locally: on each BoxMessage arrival (in the "boxes" DataChannel onmessage closure, §21.3.1) push web_sys::window().unwrap().performance().unwrap().now() — a monotonic DOMHighResTimeStamp in milliseconds — into a small VecDeque<f64> capped at ~16 entries; the badge shows the running median of the consecutive-arrival deltas. No getStats poll loop, no RTP-timestamp correlation, no extra dependency.

Why not a true send→box round-trip from getStats. A genuine "frame T sent → box for T returned" RTT would require mapping msg.rtp_ts to the wall-clock instant the streamer sent frame T — but the WebRTC statistics model exposes no outbound RTP timestamp: RTCOutboundRtpStreamStats (and the RTCSentRtpStreamStats / RTCRtpStreamStats it extends) carry no current-RTP-timestamp field to correlate against, and the local getUserMedia source has no RTP timeline at all (which is also why the streamer overlay uses requestAnimationFrame, not rVFC). The inter-arrival median captures the dominant term (inference latency, ~785 ms hybrid) honestly; the few-tens-of-milliseconds network legs it omits are noise at this scale. (RTCRemoteInboundRtpStreamStats.roundTripTime does exist, but it measures only the streamer↔SFU network hop, not the box pipeline — the wrong number for this badge.)

Viewer path
The user's browser receives a MediaStream from the server via RTCPeerConnection.set_ontrack callback's RtcTrackEvent.streams[0]; this stream is assigned to a local <video> element. End-to-end streamer-camera → viewer-screen latency is the sum of the streamer's encoder (libwebrtc default ~30–80 ms), LAN/Internet transit (~5–50 ms), the SFU re-publish (sub-ms, verified at str0m 0.20.0 src/media/writer.rs:137-181 — no buffering, immediate drain via already_happened sentinel at src/util/time_tricks.rs:52-54), the viewer browser's adaptive jitter buffer (default ~20–150 ms; lowered via RTCRtpReceiver.jitterBufferTarget = 50 in §21.2.1 below where supported), and viewer decode/render (~30 ms) — roughly ~120–250 ms typical with the jitter-buffer hint applied. The overlay is drawn via requestVideoFrameCallback when supported (it is, across the entire Section 22.1 matrix); the callback's frame-presentation tick is exactly when we want to redraw the canvas. Inside the callback, read latest_box via RwSignal::with_untracked and render. Color: saturated red #ff3030. The box arrives ~one LA cycle after the frame it describes was captured; by the time it lands at the viewer, the viewer's video is presenting a frame ~25 frames downstream — the rendered box is therefore drawn on a different frame than it was inferred from, which is exactly what the user permits.

Why not just RAF on both paths? Using rVFC on the viewer path lets the canvas redraw tick match the actual video-frame-presentation cadence (which can be lower than 60 Hz under congestion or thermal throttle on mobile), avoiding wasted draws and visible canvas-vs-video mismatch during low-framerate playback. On the streamer path the local video has effectively no jitter buffer and runs at the camera's actual cadence, so RAF (which fires at display-refresh rate) is the natural fit; rVFC offers no advantage AND has the spec-mandated rtpTimestamp == undefined for local sources.

The legacy strict-no-fallback rule on missing metadata.rtpTimestamp (a previous draft rejected the overlay loudly) is repurposed in §21.3 to apply only to the viewer path — and even there, it is now diagnostic only (the rtp_ts is used for ordering boxes on the receive side, not for sync).

21.3 The requestVideoFrameCallback extern declaration

The requestVideoFrameCallback method is not bound in web-sys version 0.3.99 (verified by reading wasm-bindgen-0.2.122/crates/web-sys/src/features/gen_HtmlVideoElement.rs). The WebAssembly client declares the binding manually. The complete extern includes the VideoFrameCallbackMetadata dictionary type with all ten fields per the WICG HTMLVideoElement.requestVideoFrameCallback() draft specification (verified live on 2026-06-01):

// wasm-client/src/extern_js.rs
use wasm_bindgen::prelude::*;

#[wasm_bindgen]
extern "C" {
    #[wasm_bindgen(extends = web_sys::HtmlVideoElement)]
    pub type HtmlVideoElementWithRVFC;

    /// JavaScript: video.requestVideoFrameCallback(callback) -> handle
    /// `cb` receives (now: DOMHighResTimeStamp, metadata: VideoFrameCallbackMetadata).
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, js_name = requestVideoFrameCallback)]
    pub fn request_video_frame_callback(
        this: &HtmlVideoElementWithRVFC,
        cb: &::js_sys::Function,
    ) -> u32;

    #[wasm_bindgen(method, js_name = cancelVideoFrameCallback)]
    pub fn cancel_video_frame_callback(this: &HtmlVideoElementWithRVFC, handle: u32);

    /// The metadata dictionary passed as the second argument to the
    /// VideoFrameRequestCallback. Per WICG video-rvfc draft, sections 2.1-2.2,
    /// the fields and their WebIDL types are:
    ///
    /// Required (6):
    ///   presentationTime:   DOMHighResTimeStamp (f64 in JS)
    ///   expectedDisplayTime: DOMHighResTimeStamp
    ///   width:              unsigned long (u32)
    ///   height:             unsigned long (u32)
    ///   mediaTime:          double (f64)
    ///   presentedFrames:    unsigned long (u32)
    ///
    /// Optional (4):
    ///   processingDuration: double
    ///   captureTime:        DOMHighResTimeStamp
    ///   receiveTime:        DOMHighResTimeStamp
    ///   rtpTimestamp:       unsigned long
    ///
    /// IMPORTANT: rtpTimestamp is the 32-bit RTP timestamp from the incoming
    /// RTP packet header. WebRTC video runs at 90 kHz per RFC 3550, so the
    /// units are 1/90000 second ticks, monotonically increasing modulo 2^32.
    /// This value matches the `data.time` MediaTime that str0m exposes on
    /// the server side via Event::MediaData — the demo server uses this for
    /// the BoxMessage.rtp_ts field, and the WASM viewer's wrap-aware
    /// "newer-rtp_ts wins" latest-wins ordering key (§21.3.1).
    pub type VideoFrameCallbackMetadata;

    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "presentationTime")]
    pub fn presentation_time(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> f64;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "expectedDisplayTime")]
    pub fn expected_display_time(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> f64;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter)]
    pub fn width(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> u32;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter)]
    pub fn height(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> u32;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "mediaTime")]
    pub fn media_time(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> f64;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "presentedFrames")]
    pub fn presented_frames(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> u32;

    // Optional fields return Option: wasm-bindgen maps JS null and
    // undefined to None; a present JS Number maps to Some(value).
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "processingDuration")]
    pub fn processing_duration(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> Option<f64>;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "captureTime")]
    pub fn capture_time(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> Option<f64>;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "receiveTime")]
    pub fn receive_time(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> Option<f64>;
    #[wasm_bindgen(method, getter, js_name = "rtpTimestamp")]
    pub fn rtp_timestamp(this: &VideoFrameCallbackMetadata) -> Option<u32>;
}

// Feature-detect at runtime. Returns Result to avoid silently masking the
// extremely unlikely Reflect::get failure case — strict no-silent-fallback:
// any unexpected JS-side failure must surface as a chained anyhow::Error,
// not as "feature absent".
pub fn has_rvfc(video: &web_sys::HtmlVideoElement) -> anyhow::Result<bool> {
    use wasm_bindgen::JsCast;
    let v = js_sys::Reflect::get(video.as_ref(), &"requestVideoFrameCallback".into())
        .map_err(crate::extern_js::js_err("Reflect::get(video, 'requestVideoFrameCallback')"))?;
    Ok(v.is_function())
}

The metadata.rtpTimestamp field is no longer load-bearing for overlay rendering. Under Strategy A (§21.2 latest-wins), the rVFC callback simply pulls the most-recent BoxMessage from latest_box at frame-presentation time and draws it; no lookup by RTP timestamp is performed. metadata.rtpTimestamp is now used only for diagnostics (e.g., the streamer's "running median round-trip-time" badge in §21.2). For the streamer path, rVFC is replaced by requestAnimationFrame entirely, because the local getUserMedia source has no RTP timeline (WICG video-rvfc spec: "absent" for non-WebRTC sources).

On the viewer path, the rVFC callback shape is:

// Inside the rVFC callback closure (called per presented video frame).
// `css_dims` is the shared Rc<Cell<(f64, f64)>> the §21.8 ResizeObserver keeps
// current; reading it here (not getBoundingClientRect per frame) avoids a
// forced layout. draw_boxes clears the canvas first, then draws (§21.9).
let (css_width, css_height) = css_dims.get();
let latest = latest_box.with_untracked(|opt| opt.clone());
match latest {
    Some(msg) => draw_boxes(&ctx, &msg, css_width, css_height, color),
    // No current box (first frame, or cleared on a stream/prompt transition
    // per §21.3.1): clear so nothing stale lingers on the new scene.
    None      => ctx.clear_rect(0.0, 0.0, css_width, css_height),
}

// Keep --video-aspect honest (§21.0.5): the viewer's track dimensions come
// from the presented-frame metadata. Update ONLY on change, so the style is
// not re-rendered every frame. For our forced square-pixel H.264 (42e01f,
// §20.1) meta.width()/height() equal the display dimensions — no pixel-aspect
// adjustment is needed (rVFC width/height carry no PAR).
let (mw, mh) = (meta.width(), meta.height());
if mw > 0 && mh > 0 && current_track_dimensions.get_untracked() != (mw, mh) {
    current_track_dimensions.set((mw, mh));   // tracked: re-renders the --video-aspect style
}

// Diagnostic only (NOT load-bearing): expose the presented frame's rtp_ts.
// reactive_graph 0.2.14 (Leptos 0.8.19's runtime) exposes update_untracked /
// write_untracked; there is no `set_untracked`.
if let Some(rtp_ts) = meta.rtp_timestamp() {
    current_frame_rtp_ts.update_untracked(|v| *v = Some(rtp_ts));
}
// Schedule the next callback (rVFC is one-shot per registration).
video.request_video_frame_callback(callback.as_ref().unchecked_ref());

Source-level verification for diagnostic-availability: Chromium third_party/blink/renderer/modules/video_rvfc/video_frame_callback_requester_impl.cc:297-303 sets the rtpTimestamp attribute whenever the underlying media::VideoFrameMetadata::rtp_timestamp has a value AND the value fits in uint32_t (both conditions hold for inbound WebRTC tracks because webrtc::VideoFrame::rtp_timestamp() returns the 32-bit RTP header field directly). Apple WebKit Source/WebCore/platform/mediastream/RealtimeIncomingVideoSource.cpp:141-142 uses the same gating. RFC 3550 fixes the WebRTC video clock at 90 kHz; the value is monotonically increasing modulo 232. So on inbound WebRTC tracks the field is always present in practice; on local getUserMedia tracks it is always absent per spec.

The strict no-fallback rule still applies to has_rvfc() at mount time (viewer path only): if the browser lacks rVFC entirely, the WebAssembly client surfaces a chained anyhow::Error rather than silently degrading. All browsers in the §22.1 matrix support rVFC as of 2026-06-02; absence indicates an unexpected browser environment.

21.2.1 RTCRtpReceiver.jitterBufferTarget — lower the viewer's playout-delay buffer where supported

libwebrtc's adaptive jitter buffer on the receiver side targets ~80–150 ms by default, growing under observed loss/jitter. For our low-latency-live-streaming goal, the viewer should hint a lower target. The RTCRtpReceiver.jitterBufferTarget property (W3C webrtc-pc §5.3, DOMHighResTimeStamp? in milliseconds, valid range [0, 4000] — RangeError outside) is a hint, not a strict cap: the spec's normative note states "If the user agent ends up using a target different from the requested one (e.g. due to network conditions or physical memory constraints), this is not reflected in the [[JitterBufferTarget]] internal slot." libwebrtc still adapts upward under observed jitter. Setting the hint to 50 ms typically saves 50–100 ms of end-to-end latency on healthy links.

Browser support as of 2026-06-02:

  • Chrome 124+ (Apr 2024) — shipped stable.
  • Firefox 115+ (Jul 2023) — shipped stable.
  • Edge 124+ (Apr 2024) — shipped stable.
  • Safari (macOS/iOS/iPadOS) — NOT in any stable Safari release yet. Added to Safari Technology Preview 242 in April 2026; expected in Safari 26.2+ stable.

We feature-detect via Reflect::has and apply if present:

use wasm_bindgen::{JsCast, JsValue};
use js_sys::Reflect;

/// Apply the jitter-buffer-target hint to a freshly-attached inbound video
/// receiver. No-op if the property is absent (Safari today). Idempotent.
/// Not a silent fallback per Section 3.1 — this is a feature-detected
/// optimization hint where absence-of-support is the documented platform
/// posture, not a silent failure.
pub fn apply_jitter_buffer_target(receiver: &web_sys::RtcRtpReceiver) -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    let key = JsValue::from_str("jitterBufferTarget");
    let has = Reflect::has(receiver.as_ref(), &key)
        .map_err(crate::extern_js::js_err("Reflect::has(receiver, 'jitterBufferTarget')"))?;
    if has {
        // 50 ms target. Hint only; libwebrtc adapts upward under observed jitter.
        Reflect::set(receiver.as_ref(), &key, &JsValue::from_f64(50.0))
            .map_err(crate::extern_js::js_err("set jitterBufferTarget=50"))?;
        tracing::info!("applied jitterBufferTarget=50 ms on inbound video receiver");
    } else {
        tracing::info!("jitterBufferTarget not supported by this browser; using libwebrtc default");
    }
    Ok(())
}

Call site: in the WebAssembly client's on_track handler (the set_ontrack callback on the viewer's RtcPeerConnection), immediately after binding the inbound video MediaStreamTrack. The handler has the RtcRtpReceiver via RtcTrackEvent::receiver().

Why not also playoutDelayHint? playoutDelayHint is the older Chrome-specific name for the same concept; jitterBufferTarget is the WICG-standardized successor (Chrome 124+ supports both). For a forward-looking design, hint via jitterBufferTarget only; the older name will eventually be deprecated.

21.3.1 DataChannel "boxes" receive path on the WebAssembly client

The server creates the "boxes" DataChannel (Section 10.7, Section 11.8 step 5). The client receives it via the RtcPeerConnection.set_ondatachannel handler, which fires when SCTP negotiation completes for the channel. The handler stores the RtcDataChannel handle in the per-PC state struct and attaches an onmessage closure.

use anyhow::Context;
use leptos::prelude::*;
use protocol::BoxMessage;

// Per-PC state struct (mirrors the closure-lifetime inventory in rtc.rs).
// The DataChannel instance and its handlers all live as long as this struct
// lives — dropping invalidates the JS-side callbacks.
pub struct DcState {
    pub dc:                 web_sys::RtcDataChannel,
    pub _open:              wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure<dyn FnMut(web_sys::Event)>,
    pub _msg:               wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure<dyn FnMut(web_sys::MessageEvent)>,
    pub _close:             wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure<dyn FnMut(web_sys::CloseEvent)>,
    pub _err:               wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure<dyn FnMut(web_sys::Event)>,
    /// The single latest BoxMessage. Strategy A (latest-wins) per §21.2:
    /// LA inference takes ~800 ms hybrid; by the time a box for frame X
    /// arrives, the video has advanced ~25 frames past X. Per-frame
    /// timestamp matching would mean the box for X never finds the frame
    /// it describes — viewers would see no boxes at all. Instead we always
    /// render the most recent BoxMessage on whatever frame is currently
    /// being presented, exactly as the user's stated goal allows ("no need
    /// for bounding boxes to come in at the same time as the frame being
    /// presented"). The `rtp_ts` field on BoxMessage is retained for
    /// diagnostics and for ordering (newer rtp_ts wins on the rare DC
    /// reorder), not for sync.
    pub latest_box:         RwSignal<Option<BoxMessage>>,
}

// Attaching the channel:
pub fn attach_boxes_dc(
    dc: web_sys::RtcDataChannel,
    latest_box: RwSignal<Option<BoxMessage>>,
    last_error: RwSignal<Option<String>>,
) -> DcState {
    // The "boxes" channel is always JSON text frames. Set binary_type defensively
    // so any unexpected binary frame surfaces as an as_string() == None case
    // we explicitly reject.
    dc.set_binary_type(web_sys::RtcDataChannelType::Arraybuffer);

    let buf_for_msg = latest_box;
    let err_for_msg = last_error;
    let on_msg = wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure::<dyn FnMut(web_sys::MessageEvent)>::new(
        move |event: web_sys::MessageEvent| {
            let text = match event.data().as_string() {
                Some(s) => s,
                None => {
                    err_for_msg.set(Some(
                        "boxes DataChannel received non-text frame; protocol violation, \
                         tearing down connection".to_string()
                    ));
                    return;
                }
            };
            let msg: BoxMessage = match protocol::parse_box_message(&text) {
                Ok(m) => m,
                Err(e) => {
                    err_for_msg.set(Some(format!("parse BoxMessage: {e:#}")));
                    return;
                }
            };
            // Strategy A: keep the latest BoxMessage only. On the rare case
            // a reordered datagram delivers an older box AFTER a newer one
            // (unordered DataChannel, unreliable), `wrapping_sub` lets us
            // detect this and reject — newer-rtp_ts wins, never overwrite
            // backwards. Note that under stop-and-wait LA + LAN transport,
            // reordering is essentially impossible; this guard is defense.
            buf_for_msg.update(|slot| {
                let accept = match slot {
                    None => true,
                    Some(cur) => {
                        // Treat msg as "newer" if (msg.rtp_ts - cur.rtp_ts)
                        // mod 2^32 is in the forward half (≤ 2^31). This is
                        // RFC 1982 §3.2 serial-number-arithmetic sequence-comparison
                        // for u32 RTP timestamps; tolerates the ~13-hour
                        // wrap-around cleanly.
                        let diff = msg.rtp_ts.wrapping_sub(cur.rtp_ts);
                        diff != 0 && diff < 0x8000_0000
                    }
                };
                if accept {
                    *slot = Some(msg);
                }
            });
        }
    );
    dc.set_onmessage(Some(on_msg.as_ref().unchecked_ref()));

    let on_open  = wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure::<dyn FnMut(_)>::new(move |_e: web_sys::Event| {
        leptos::logging::log!("boxes DataChannel open");
    });
    dc.set_onopen(Some(on_open.as_ref().unchecked_ref()));

    let err_for_close = last_error;
    let on_close = wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure::<dyn FnMut(_)>::new(move |e: web_sys::CloseEvent| {
        err_for_close.set(Some(format!(
            "boxes DataChannel closed: code={code}, reason={reason}",
            code = e.code(), reason = e.reason()
        )));
    });
    dc.set_onclose(Some(on_close.as_ref().unchecked_ref()));

    let err_for_err = last_error;
    let on_err = wasm_bindgen::closure::Closure::<dyn FnMut(_)>::new(move |_e: web_sys::Event| {
        err_for_err.set(Some("boxes DataChannel error (see browser console)".to_string()));
    });
    dc.set_onerror(Some(on_err.as_ref().unchecked_ref()));

    DcState { dc, _open: on_open, _msg: on_msg, _close: on_close, _err: on_err, latest_box }
}

Why latest-wins instead of frame-keyed lookup. The user explicitly granted permission for boxes and frames to be desynchronized: "no need for the bounding boxes to come in at the same time as the frame being presented." Under that constraint, frame-keyed lookup is over-engineered AND broken at realistic LA latency: LocateAnything-3B's hybrid mode takes ~785 ms; by the time the box for frame X arrives at the viewer, the video has advanced ~24 frames past X. An exact-rtp_ts BTreeMap::get would never find a match — boxes would pile up unused and viewers would see nothing. Latest-wins draws the most-recent inference result on whatever frame the rVFC callback (or RAF, for the streamer's local source) is currently presenting; the staleness is honestly one full inference cycle.

Wrap-aware comparison. The 32-bit RTP timestamp at 90 kHz wraps modulo 2^32 every ~13.25 hours. The accept-newer-only guard uses RFC 1982 §3.2 serial-number arithmetic: (new - current) mod 2^32 < 2^31 means "new is forward of current in the cyclic order". This handles the wrap edge correctly without needing an explicit "did we wrap" flag — at cur = 0xFFFF_FF00, new = 0x0000_0100, the wrapping subtraction yields 0x200 which is well under 0x8000_0000, so new is correctly accepted as forward across the wrap.

Protocol-violation policy. Any binary frame on the "boxes" channel surfaces a loud error to the user and tears down the connection (in the receive callback above, we surface to last_error but do not actively close the channel from JS; the reconnect loop will pick that up on next signaling cycle). Any frame that fails JSON parsing surfaces the chained-anyhow parse error. Neither is silently dropped.

Resetting the slot. latest_box is set back to None whenever the client leaves the live view — on ResumeExpired and on a user-initiated Bye/Release (the §21.10.0 transitions that revert to the 7-card prompt-builder), and on a fresh Claim — so a box inferred for the previous prompt or scene never lingers over a new one. Because the per-frame draw clears the canvas whenever latest_box is None (§21.3, §21.9), the overlay goes blank immediately on reset rather than freezing the last detections.

21.4 playsinline attribute handling

The playsInline setter is not bound in web-sys 0.3.99 (verified by reading the same file). Set the attribute via Leptos's view! macro (which uses setAttribute under the hood) or via Element::set_attribute("playsinline", "") imperatively. Required for Apple iOS Safari to prevent the <video> element from going fullscreen on play.

21.5 Video element required attributes

Every <video> element in the application must have:

  • playsinline — required on Apple iOS Safari to keep playback inline. Set as an HTML attribute (Leptos: playsinline="" in the view! macro, or element.set_attribute("playsinline", "") imperatively).
  • autoplay — so playback starts without an explicit .play() call. Set via Leptos's property-binding syntax prop:autoplay=true in the view! macro.
  • muted set to true via the JavaScript IDL property (not just the HTML attribute). Apple iOS Safari's autoplay heuristic checks the IDL property; setting only the HTML attribute is insufficient on some Safari versions. Use Leptos's property-binding syntax prop:muted=true in the view! macro; this compiles to HtmlMediaElement::set_muted(true) (verified at web-sys-0.3.99/src/features/gen_HtmlMediaElement.rs:298). Even though our MediaStream has no audio (audio: false in getUserMedia), Apple iOS Safari requires this signal anyway.

Canonical Leptos view! shape:

view! {
    <video
        playsinline=""
        prop:autoplay=true
        prop:muted=true
        class="streamer-video"
        node_ref=video_ref
    />
}

The video_ref is a NodeRef<leptos::html::Video> created with NodeRef::new(); on mount, the imperative HtmlVideoElement::set_src_object(Some(&stream)) attaches the MediaStream to the element.

21.6 Camera enumeration and picker user interface

The cross-platform camera-picker pattern (no per-platform branching):

  1. On page load, call navigator.mediaDevices.enumerateDevices(). Filter results to kind === "videoinput". If all returned MediaDeviceInfo.label fields are empty strings (which they are before permission is granted), render the picker with placeholder text ("Camera 1", "Camera 2", ...) and a "Detect cameras" call-to-action button.
  2. On the call-to-action button, call navigator.mediaDevices.getUserMedia({ video: true, audio: false }) with default constraints. This triggers the browser's permission prompt against the default camera.
  3. On success: re-call enumerateDevices() — labels are now populated. Re-render the picker with real names. Keep the obtained stream live (do not stop it); reuse it.
  4. When the user picks a specific device from the dropdown: if the selected device identifier matches the currently-active track's device, no-op. Otherwise: call getUserMedia({ video: { deviceId: { exact: selectedId }, width: { ideal: 1280, max: 1280 }, height: { ideal: 720, max: 720 } }, audio: false }) — carrying the SAME Level 3.1 capture ceiling as the initial constraints (§20.2), because the forced 42e01f binds a switched-to camera exactly as it binds the first one. Then re-validate the new track's dimensions with the SAME check_capture_dimensions helper (§20.2) before swapping, and swap the WebRTC track in-place via the Rust pattern below (the JavaScript-style pc.getSenders().find(|s| s.track.kind === "video").replaceTrack(newTrack) shorthand sometimes seen in docs is JS pseudocode, not valid Rust — the Rust shape is more explicit): 
    use anyhow::Context;
use wasm_bindgen::JsCast;

// The deviceId-constrained getUserMedia above resolves to `new_stream`.
let new_track: web_sys::MediaStreamTrack = new_stream
    .get_video_tracks().get(0)
    .dyn_into().map_err(js_err("camera-switch MediaStream has no video track"))?;

// Re-run the SAME capture-dimension policy as the initial path (§20.2): the forced
// 42e01f Level 3.1 ceiling binds the switched-to camera too. On refusal, stop the
// NEW track and abort the switch — the existing track stays live, so the session
// keeps streaming on the working camera while the error surfaces to the user.
let settings = new_track.get_settings();
let nw = settings.get_width().ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!(
    "MediaTrackSettings.width missing after camera switch"))?;
let nh = settings.get_height().ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!(
    "MediaTrackSettings.height missing after camera switch"))?;
match check_capture_dimensions(nw, nh) {
    Err(e)        => { new_track.stop(); return Err(e); }
    Ok(Some(msg)) => last_warning.set(Some(msg)),
    Ok(None)      => {}
}

// Iterate pc.get_senders() (returns js_sys::Array of RtcRtpSender JsValues),
// find the one with kind == "video", call replace_track returning Promise.
let senders: js_sys::Array = pc.get_senders();
let target_sender: web_sys::RtcRtpSender = (0..senders.length())
    .filter_map(|i| {
        let s: web_sys::RtcRtpSender = senders.get(i).unchecked_into();
        match s.track() {
            Some(t) if t.kind() == "video" => Some(s),
            _ => None,
        }
    })
    .next()
    .ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!("no video sender on PeerConnection"))?;

let promise = target_sender.replace_track(Some(&new_track));
wasm_bindgen_futures::JsFuture::from(promise).await
    .map_err(js_err("RtcRtpSender::replaceTrack(new camera track)"))?;

old_track.stop();
  5. RTCRtpSender.replaceTrack works for mid-call camera switches without SDP renegotiation when the new track has the same kind and similar parameters (per Mozilla Developer Network documentation; Baseline since January 2020).

Track addition at session start. Earlier drafts of this plan wrote pc.add_track(track, &[&stream]) as if it accepted a slice. The actual web-sys 0.3.99 binding signature (verified at web-sys 0.3.99 src/features/gen_RtcPeerConnection.rs:521) is:

pub fn add_track(
    this: &RtcPeerConnection,
    track: &MediaStreamTrack,
    stream: &MediaStream,
    more_streams: &::js_sys::Array,  // variadic "extra streams"
) -> RtcRtpSender;

So either pass an empty js_sys::Array:

let extra_streams = js_sys::Array::new();
let sender: web_sys::RtcRtpSender = pc.add_track(&video_track, &media_stream, &extra_streams);

Or use the no-extras-streams form pc.add_track_0(&video_track, &media_stream) (verified at web-sys 0.3.99 src/features/gen_RtcPeerConnection.rs:538-542). The _0 suffix means "zero extra streams", not "zero streams" — a MediaStream is still required as the second positional argument because the underlying browser API associates every track with at least one stream by spec. The _N suffix throughout web-sys's generated bindings counts ADDITIONAL extra-stream args; add_track_1 takes track + stream + one more stream, etc. Our SFU does not need extra-stream associations, so add_track_0 with a single MediaStream is the cleanest call.

21.6.1 Camera-permission denial branch (strict, loud)

If the user clicks "Block" (or "Don't Allow") in the browser's permission prompt at step 2 of the cross-platform picker pattern, getUserMedia rejects with a NotAllowedError. The WebAssembly client must NOT silently retry or fall back to a placeholder camera. Strict behavior:

  1. Surface the chained-anyhow error string in the error banner: "Camera permission denied: NotAllowedError".
  2. Render the help subpage content from Section 21.13 inline beneath the banner, but with the iOS-cert-specific wording replaced by the platform-appropriate permission-revocation instructions: macOS Safari (Settings → Websites → Camera), Google Chrome desktop (lock icon → Site Settings → Camera), Android Chrome (browser-app-level permission in OS settings), Apple iOS Safari (Settings → Apple Safari → Camera → Ask).
  3. The "Claim Streamer" button remains visible but is now in a disabled visual state with a tooltip on hover: "Camera access required. Update browser permissions and reload."
  4. Do not retry getUserMedia until the user reloads the page. A retry while permission is still denied would just re-trigger the same error and gives no progress signal; the user must change the platform-level permission first.
  5. Other getUserMedia failure modes (NotFoundError: no camera; NotReadableError: hardware busy; OverconstrainedError: even ideal constraints couldn't be honored, extremely rare with our ideal-only constraints) follow the same loud-banner pattern with class-specific remediation copy.

What this is NOT: a silent attempt to keep streaming a single static frame, or a degraded "screenshot mode", or any other fallback path. The user denied camera access; we honor that and tell them clearly.

21.7 Canvas overlay positioning

Parent <div> with position: relative. The <video> is the natural-flow child sizing the parent. The <canvas> is position: absolute; inset: 0; width: 100%; height: 100%; pointer-events: none;. The overlay layout's CSS lives in wasm-client/styles.css (external CSS file; no inline styles per the CSP discipline of Section 16).

21.8 ResizeObserver and device-pixel-ratio changes

Observe the parent <div> (not the video element, because the video may letterbox inside its layout box). On every resize entry, recompute the canvas backing-store dimensions, publish the current CSS size into the shared css_dims: Rc<Cell<(f64, f64)>> that the draw callback reads (§21.3, §21.9), and re-apply the device-pixel-ratio transform:

let dpr = window.device_pixel_ratio();
css_dims.set((css_width, css_height));              // shared with the rVFC/RAF draw callback
canvas.set_width((css_width  * dpr) as u32);        // set_width/set_height RESET the 2D context
canvas.set_height((css_height * dpr) as u32);       // transform to identity (WHATWG bitmap-resize),
ctx.scale(dpr, dpr).map_err(js_err("ctx.scale"))?;  // so this scale does NOT accumulate across resizes

ResizeObserver does NOT fire on a device-pixel-ratio change when the CSS box is unchanged — e.g. dragging the window to a display with a different DPR, or browser page-zoom — leaving the backing store stale (blurry, or mis-scaled boxes) until some unrelated resize. So also register a self-re-arming matchMedia(&format!("(resolution: {dpr}dppx)")) change listener; on fire, re-run the sizing block above (it re-reads device_pixel_ratio(), which resets the transform via set_width) and re-arm the listener against the new ratio. Both the ResizeObserver and this media-query listener are owned closures in the §21.11 inventory.

21.9 Bounding-box coordinate transform

Boxes arrive normalized in [0.0, 1.0]. The WebAssembly client multiplies by the current CSS width and height of the canvas (css_width/css_height — read from the shared cell the §21.8 ResizeObserver keeps current, see §21.3, never getBoundingClientRect per frame). draw_boxes clears the whole canvas first, so the previous inference's shapes never ghost; an abstained reply (empty boxes and points) therefore leaves a clean, blank overlay. The per-frame caller (viewer rVFC / streamer RAF) calls this every presented frame, and clears directly when latest_box is None (§21.3). Note: box is a reserved keyword in Rust; the local binding is named bb:

// Clear the whole canvas in CSS-pixel space (the ctx is already DPR-scaled,
// §21.8) BEFORE drawing — otherwise each frame's shapes paint over the last
// and the overlay smears.
ctx.clear_rect(0.0, 0.0, css_width as f64, css_height as f64);

for bb in box_message.boxes.iter() {
    let x = bb.x1 * css_width;
    let y = bb.y1 * css_height;
    let w = (bb.x2 - bb.x1) * css_width;
    let h = (bb.y2 - bb.y1) * css_height;
    ctx.stroke_rect(x as f64, y as f64, w as f64, h as f64);
}

// The `point` template (PromptTask::Point) returns points, not boxes (§10.7);
// render each as a small crosshair so that template is not silently blank.
// Points are normalized [0.0, 1.0] in the same space as box corners.
for pt in box_message.points.iter() {
    let (cx, cy, r) = ((pt.x * css_width) as f64, (pt.y * css_height) as f64, 6.0_f64);
    ctx.begin_path();
    ctx.move_to(cx - r, cy); ctx.line_to(cx + r, cy);
    ctx.move_to(cx, cy - r); ctx.line_to(cx, cy + r);
    ctx.stroke();
}

Stroke styling: line width 2.0 pixels in CSS pixels. Stroke color #ff3030 (saturated red) for viewer-side; #dd5050 (desaturated red) for streamer-side. Optional label drawn above the box with a filled rectangle background (same color at 70 percent alpha) and white 12-pixel sans-serif text.

Accessibility. The canvas overlay is purely visual (pointer-events: none, no DOM semantics), so it is invisible to assistive technology. To leave a non-visual signal, the detection count (the same value the §21.0.6 pill shows) is mirrored into a visually-hidden aria-live="polite" region that updates only when the count changes — not every inference cycle, which would be too chatty for a screen reader.

21.10 WebSocket reconnect on the WebAssembly client

No fixed maximum-consecutive-errors cap. Earlier draft of this plan capped at 10 consecutive errors, after which the user was shown "Connection lost — please refresh the page". The maximum cumulative back-off across those 10 retries is approximately 55 seconds, which is shorter than the 1-3-minute 5 AM router cycle that this design must "survive". Capping below the expected outage window means every browser tab would display "please refresh" before the outage ends — exactly the failure the design exists to prevent. The strict-correctness policy is: never give up automatically; keep retrying with a capped back-off forever; show the user an obvious reconnecting-state UI; let the user explicitly opt out if they want.

Mirroring the reference Python client's pattern at /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/examples/reference_client.py:213-225, 248, 268-272, but tuned for the browser:

  • Initial delay: 500 milliseconds (Python reference uses 3 seconds; in the browser, 3 seconds feels broken).
  • Multiplier: 2.
  • Back-off cap: 30 seconds (each subsequent retry waits at most 30 s, indefinitely).
  • No retry-count cap. The reconnect loop runs forever as long as the page is open. Specifically: if the page is open, we are trying.
  • Jitter: plus or minus 250 milliseconds uniform (smears arrival times when N clients all reconnect after a server restart). Source: js_sys::Math::random() on the WebAssembly target (no getrandom WASM build dependency; jitter doesn't need cryptographic quality).
  • Graceful-close (WebSocket Close codes 1000 and 1001) resets the back-off floor to the 500-millisecond initial delay so that an immediate planned reconnect (e.g., the server restarted gracefully) does not have to climb the back-off ladder unnecessarily.
  • User-visible state: the application's ConnState reactive signal goes to Reconnecting { attempt: u32, last_error: String } on every retry; the connection-state banner in the user interface always shows the current retry attempt and the last chained-anyhow error message. The banner has a "Stop trying" button (rendered after attempt 5) that, if clicked, transitions ConnState to Stopped and the user has to manually click "Try again" to resume the reconnect loop. This gives the user explicit, opt-in giving up — never silent automated giving up.

What the user sees during the 5 AM router cycle, with this design: at 05:00:00 the connection drops. At 05:00:00.5 the WebAssembly client begins retrying. Each retry fails until connectivity returns at 05:01:30 (or whenever). At that point, the next retry succeeds; the application transitions to Reconnecting { ... } → Connecting → Connected; the WebSocket reconnect loop survives the entire outage — the user sees "Reconnecting (attempt 12, last error: <chained>) — Stop trying" throughout, then "Connected" immediately afterward, with no "please refresh" prompt ever. Ownership, however, is a separate guarantee. The Finite State Machine reaches Idle roughly 35 seconds into the outage (5 s RTP_TIMEOUT → Draining, then the 30 s DRAIN_TIMEOUT → Idle, per §11.2); because the 1–3 minute router cycle far exceeds the 30 s resume window, the post-outage ResumeSession lands on an Idle FSM and returns ResumeExpired, so the former streamer re-claims from the 7-card prompt grid (§21.10.0 item 5). This is correct per the "if anybody disconnects, the server cleanly reverts to a mode where anybody can take ownership" requirement (§2) — a streamer who genuinely vanished for minutes does not hold the single slot hostage. Ownership survives only drops shorter than DRAIN_TIMEOUT (~30 s) — a brief blip or a Wi-Fi↔cellular handover — NOT the full router cycle.

21.10.0 ResumeSession lifecycle on the WebAssembly client

The WebAssembly client holds the current session identifier in an RwSignal<Option<String>> named session_id, scoped to the top-level App component. Lifecycle rules, strict:

  1. First-ever WebSocket connect for a page session: session_id starts None. The WebAssembly client does NOT send SignalMessage::ResumeSession {}; it just opens the WebSocket and waits for the user to interact with the prompt-builder grid.
  2. On successful Claim: the server replies SignalMessage::ResumeOk { session_id: id } with the freshly-minted ID (Section 10.6); the client sets session_id.set(Some(id)).
  3. On WebSocket close (graceful 1000/1001 OR error close): the reconnect loop (Section 21.10) reopens a new WebSocket. After the open completes, if session_id is Some(id), the client sends SignalMessage::ResumeSession { session_id: id } as the very first message. The server replies either ResumeOk (ownership preserved) or ResumeExpired (server gave the slot to someone else, or the drain timer fired).
  4. On ResumeOk: the client retains session_id and follows Option α: tear down the old RTCPeerConnection, build a fresh one, send a new SdpOffer.
  5. On ResumeExpired: the client clears session_id.set(None) and reverts the user interface to the 7-card prompt-builder grid.
  6. On user-initiated Bye / Release: the client clears session_id.set(None) immediately, before sending the SignalMessage::Bye {} to the server.
  7. On page navigation away: Leptos's cleanup runs App's on_cleanup hook; session_id's memory is freed alongside the rest of the application state. The server's session-grace window (per Section 11.2's DRAIN_TIMEOUT of 30 seconds — after a streamer WebSocket close, the FSM transitions to Draining and holds the session_id for the drain duration) handles the case where the user comes back: if they return within the 30-second drain window AND the FSM has not yet transitioned to Idle, their ResumeSession request lands on a Draining FSM and is granted (the FSM cancels the drain and re-enters Claimed with the same session_id, awaiting the fresh post-Option-α RTP — §11.6.1); if they return after 30 seconds (the FSM is back to Idle), ResumeExpired fires. The 30-second window deliberately covers iPhone WiFi↔cellular handover (~1–3 s re-attach + ~21.5 s ICE consent freshness), so a streamer who switches networks mid-stream does not lose their slot.

Where session_id is NOT persisted: we deliberately do NOT use sessionStorage or localStorage. The session-id is in-memory only. Reasons: (a) sessionStorage adds a DOM-storage API surface that requires CSP connect-src-like considerations and Permissions-Policy entries; (b) localStorage would leak the session-id across reloads, which doesn't compose with the server's session-grace semantics. In-memory only.

21.10.1 RTCPeerConnection lifecycle across WebSocket reconnects (Option B)

Critical design pattern (verified by source-level research on 2026-06-01 against W3C WebRTC specification §4.3.1 + §4.4.1.4, IETF RFC 9429 §3.2 + §5.6, Chromium libwebrtc pc/sdp_offer_answer.cc:2128-3434, Mozilla gecko-dev JsepSessionImpl.cpp:954-1002, and Apple WebKit RTCPeerConnection.cpp:432-462):
  1. The browser's RTCPeerConnection object has no link to the signaling WebSocket. Per W3C §4.1, "the signaling channel is provided by unspecified means." There is no spec-mandated nor implementation-imposed timeout between setLocalDescription(offer) and setRemoteDescription(answer) — verified absent across all three engines.
  2. Even though the spec would PERMIT preserving a single RTCPeerConnection across signaling-WebSocket reconnects (option A), we deliberately do NOT do this. Reason: the user's stated preference "I hate connections — it makes it so hard to make sure things are correct" plus "strict correctness, no fallbacks." Option A introduces three correlated state machines (browser signaling state, WASM client's WebSocket view, server's session-grace map) that must remain coherent across asynchronous partial failures.
  3. On every WebSocket reconnect, the WebAssembly client tears down its RTCPeerConnection via pc.close() (W3C §4.4.1, idempotent) and discards the JavaScript reference. The new WebSocket connection sends SignalMessage::ResumeSession { session_id }; on ResumeOk, the client constructs a fresh RTCPeerConnection, calls force_h264_baseline_only() on its video transceiver (Section 20.1.2), createOffer(), setLocalDescription, and sends the new SdpOffer over the new WebSocket. The server treats it as a fresh negotiation. On ResumeExpired, the client transitions the user interface back to the 7-card prompt-builder grid for a fresh claim.
  4. Cost of this approach: one extra ICE-gathering round-trip per reconnect (a few hundred milliseconds typically). Benefit: server has no stored SDP-answer state, the protocol's ResumeOk message carries no SDP data, and the WASM client never reasons about "did I already receive the answer for the previous offer?"
  5. ICE candidates the server sent before the WebSocket died are lost in transit; the server resends them by performing a fresh ICE-candidate gathering on the new RTCPeerConnection created server-side as part of the new SdpAnswer. Per RFC 9429 §3.5.2 and §4.1.19, ICE candidates may flow at any time after the relevant description exists.
  6. ICE restart was considered and rejected. The WebRTC specification (W3C §4.4.2 line 3594, the RTCPeerConnection.restartIce() method) plus RFC 8445 §9 plus the str0m 0.20 API at src/change/sdp.rs:450-469 (the ice_restart(keep_local_candidates: bool) method) plus str0m's auto-detection of remote ICE restart at src/change/sdp.rs:723-745 all combine to make ICE restart technically supported across the device matrix (Chrome 77+, Firefox 70+, Safari macOS 14.1+, Safari iOS 14.5+). On a successful ICE restart, the existing RTCPeerConnection object's accumulated state (transceivers, senders, statistics, DTLS keys) is preserved and only the ICE credentials and candidate pairs are renegotiated — saving approximately 50-150 milliseconds of Datagram Transport Layer Security handshake time per reconnect. We deliberately do NOT use this mechanism, for two reasons: (a) it re-introduces the correlated state-machine hazard (browser signaling state, WebSocket survival, ICE state) that Option B is designed to eliminate; and (b) the 50-150 milliseconds of savings amortizes against the 1-3 minute outage that triggered the reconnect, so the savings are negligible relative to the user-visible event. If future operational data shows mobile-hop reconnects are noticeably slow, ICE restart can be added as a focused optimization, but it does not pay for itself in the current design.

21.11 Closure lifetime management — complete inventory

Do not call .forget() on Rust Closure instances except in the specific one-shot case documented below. Forgetting permanently leaks the closure into the JavaScript garbage collector's roots. Instead, store the closure in a state struct that lives at least as long as the JavaScript-side handle that holds the function reference. Dropping a closure invalidates the JavaScript-side callback; a subsequent JS-side invocation throws "closure invoked recursively or after being dropped" (verified at /tmp/wasm-bindgen-src/src/convert/closures.rs:92). For our discipline, the closure drops at the same time the JS-side object holding it drops, so the invocation-after-drop case never arises.

Complete inventory of closures the WebAssembly client creates, with owning struct and lifetime:

ClosureOwning structLifetime
WebSocket onopen / onmessage / onclose / onerrorWsHandles { _open: Closure<...>, _msg: Closure<...>, _close: Closure<...>, _err: Closure<...> }One WebSocket connection (dropped on connect_once return; the WS is closed first)
RtcPeerConnection ontrackPcHandles { _ontrack: Closure<...>, ... }One PC (dropped on pc.close())
RtcPeerConnection ondatachannelSame PcHandlesSame
RtcPeerConnection onicecandidateSame PcHandlesSame
RtcPeerConnection oniceconnectionstatechangeSame PcHandlesSame
RtcDataChannel onopen / onmessage / onclose / onerror (the "boxes" channel)DcHandles { _open: Closure<...>, _msg: Closure<...>, _close: Closure<...>, _err: Closure<...> }One DataChannel
ResizeObserver callback (canvas sizing)ObserverHandles { _resize: Closure<...> }One video pane component
requestVideoFrameCallback per-frame callback (viewer overlay)RvfcHandles { _cb: Closure<...>, handle: u32 }One viewer pane (cancelled via cancel_video_frame_callback(handle) on unmount)
requestAnimationFrame redraw loop (streamer overlay — local source has no RTP timeline, §21.2)RafHandles { _cb: Closure<...>, handle: i32 }One streamer pane (cancelled via cancel_animation_frame(handle) on unmount / camera switch)
matchMedia("(resolution: …dppx)") change listener (device-pixel-ratio change, §21.8)Same ObserverHandles as the ResizeObserverOne video pane (re-armed against the new ratio on each fire)
setTimeout callback for reconnect-backoff sleepOne-shot: Closure::once_into_js(...)Self-leaks into JS GC; fires exactly once and is collected

The setTimeout entry is the only legitimate once_into_js case in the entire WebAssembly client. Per /tmp/wasm-bindgen-src/src/closure.rs documentation, Closure::once_into_js is exactly designed for "run this exactly once via JS callback then let the JS GC reclaim it" semantics. Using it elsewhere would leak.

21.11.1 The reconnect-backoff sleep_ms helper (load-bearing for Section 21.10)

WebAssembly has no tokio::sleep. The reconnect-backoff loop in Section 21.10 (500 ms → 30 s capped, retries forever) needs a sleep primitive. The plan does NOT add gloo-timers to the dependency set; instead it uses a hand-wrapped Promise + setTimeout pattern via already-pinned web-sys, js-sys, and wasm-bindgen-futures:

use anyhow::Context;
use wasm_bindgen::{closure::Closure, JsCast, JsValue};
use wasm_bindgen_futures::JsFuture;
use js_sys::Promise;

/// Suspends the current Tokio-free async task for the requested
/// number of milliseconds, using a Promise that resolves from a
/// browser-scheduled setTimeout callback. Returns Err if the
/// underlying setTimeout call fails, which should not happen in
/// practice for non-pathological delay values.
pub async fn sleep_ms(ms: i32) -> anyhow::Result<()> {
    let window = web_sys::window()
        .ok_or_else(|| anyhow::anyhow!("no window object available (running outside browser?)"))?;

    // The schedule-and-resolve dance lives in an Rc-shared error slot so the
    // outer body of sleep_ms can convert any setTimeout failure into a
    // chained-anyhow result — STRICT no-expect in runtime; Promise::new's
    // executor cannot return Result directly, so we stash the error.
    let outer_err: std::rc::Rc<std::cell::RefCell<Option<String>>>
        = std::rc::Rc::new(std::cell::RefCell::new(None));
    let outer_err_for_executor = outer_err.clone();
    let promise = Promise::new(&mut |resolve, _reject| {
        // Closure::once_into_js is the single legitimate use of leaking-to-JS-GC
        // in our entire WebAssembly client: the timer fires exactly once, the
        // closure body invokes resolve(JsValue::NULL) which completes the Promise,
        // and the JS GC reclaims the closure shortly afterward.
        let cb = Closure::once_into_js(move || {
            let _ = resolve.call0(&JsValue::NULL);
        });
        if let Err(e) = window.set_timeout_with_callback_and_timeout_and_arguments_0(
            cb.unchecked_ref(), ms,
        ) {
            // Browser refused to schedule (pathological delay value or
            // exhausted timer table). Stash the error string so the outer
            // body can propagate it after the Promise resolves to never.
            *outer_err_for_executor.borrow_mut() = Some(format!("{e:?}"));
            // Best effort: resolve the Promise immediately so we don't hang.
            // The outer body checks outer_err.borrow().is_some() after awaiting
            // and returns Err if so.
            let _ = resolve.call0(&JsValue::NULL);
        }
    });

    JsFuture::from(promise).await
        .map_err(crate::extern_js::js_err("sleep_ms Promise"))?;

    // Check the stashed setTimeout error, if any.
    if let Some(err) = outer_err.borrow_mut().take() {
        anyhow::bail!("set_timeout_with_callback failed: {err}");
    }
    Ok(())
}

The error-propagation dance via an Rc<RefCell<Option<String>>> is required because Promise::new's executor cannot return a Result directly. The dance stashes the error and resolves the Promise immediately on setTimeout failure; the outer sleep_ms body checks the stash after awaiting. This honors Section 4.1's hard no-.expect rule.

Used in the reconnect loop as:

let mut consecutive_errors = 0u32;
let mut delay_ms: i32 = 500;
loop {
    if let Err(e) = connect_once().await {
        consecutive_errors += 1;
        last_error.set(Some(format!("{e:#}")));
        conn_state.set(ConnState::Reconnecting {
            attempt: consecutive_errors,
            last_error: format!("{e:#}"),
        });
        let jitter: i32 = ((js_sys::Math::random() * 500.0) as i32) - 250;
        let sleep_with_jitter = (delay_ms + jitter).max(100);
        sleep_ms(sleep_with_jitter).await
            .with_context(|| format!("backoff sleep before attempt {}", consecutive_errors + 1))?;
        delay_ms = (delay_ms.saturating_mul(2)).min(30_000);
    } else {
        // Graceful close (1000/1001) — reset backoff floor.
        delay_ms = 500;
        consecutive_errors = 0;
    }
}

21.12 Boot-time diagnostics — corrected from the earlier three-stage form

Important correction (verified by source-level research on 2026-06-01): earlier drafts of this section had three stages including a check on window.is_secure_context() to detect cert-warning click-through. That check is dead code: per the WHATWG Secure Contexts specification (cited inversely in Section 22.2), isSecureContext returns true for any https:// origin regardless of certificate validation state — the algorithm checks scheme, not cert validity. Since our service only serves on https://<public-host>:8443/ with a self-signed cert, this check would always return true for any browser that successfully loaded our page (a browser that rejected the cert never loads the page at all, so the WASM never runs to perform the check). The check has been removed.

The actual diagnostics, in order:

  1. Mount-time: read window.location.hash. If empty, render an explainer page: "This demo requires a per-session secret in the URL fragment (e.g., https://demo.example.com:8443/#YOUR_SECRET_HERE). Without it, no API endpoint is reachable. See operator for the current secret." Do NOT show the prompt-builder grid; do NOT attempt any HTTP request (which would 401 anyway).
  2. Mount-time: if window.navigator.media_devices() returns None (i.e., navigator.mediaDevices === undefined on the JS side, indicating a non-secure context that somehow loaded — for example a manually-typed http:// URL — or an extremely old browser), render the cert-acceptance-help banner with link to ?help=ios-cert for Apple iOS specifics. Reaching this branch from our HTTPS-only server is operationally unlikely but the check is cheap.
  3. Lazily, on user gesture (the "Detect cameras" button click): call getUserMedia({video: true, audio: false}). If it rejects with NotAllowedError, follow the Section 21.6.1 permission-denial branch. If it rejects with NotFoundError / NotReadableError / OverconstrainedError, follow the same loud-banner pattern with class-specific copy.

21.13 Apple iOS Safari help subpage

Render at ?help=ios-cert a step-by-step instruction subpage with screenshots showing:

  1. "You'll see a warning that says 'This Connection Is Not Private'."
  2. "Tap 'Show Details'."
  3. "Tap 'visit this website'."
  4. "Confirm 'Visit Website' in the popup."
  5. "Camera permission will be requested next."
  6. Note: "On Apple iOS, this acceptance is session-only and will be requested again on every tab close and every cert regeneration (~27 months)."

22.2 Critical compatibility notes

  • Apple iOS Safari's "Show Details → visit this website" cert click-through is session-only. Lost on tab close, app switch (long enough for WebKit to reclaim the session), or browser restart. The only durable trust mechanism on Apple iOS is installing a Configuration Profile (.mobileconfig file) under Settings → General → About → Certificate Trust Settings, which is outside the basic flow.
  • Every browser loses the cert trust decision when our cert is regenerated (cert fingerprint changes). This will happen approximately every 27 months at the operator's discretion when the cert approaches its 824-day notAfter.
  • Google Chrome desktop running under enterprise management with SSLErrorOverrideAllowed=false policy cannot reach the demo at all: the "Proceed (Insecure)" link is hidden and the hidden thisisunsafe keystroke bypass is also disabled. Document this for IT-admin awareness in the operator-facing README.
  • All current browsers in the Section 22.1 matrix implement requestVideoFrameCallback: Chrome / Safari / Chromium-on-iOS / Firefox 132+ desktop (released October 2024, Bugzilla 1919367) / Firefox for Android 150+. The WebAssembly client still feature-detects via has_rvfc() (Section 21.3) at mount time — if it ever runs against a browser without rVFC (an older Firefox or a future browser variant), it propagates a chained anyhow::Error to the user-facing error banner instead of silently falling back. Strict no-silent-fallback per Section 3.
  • Apple iOS Safari's enumerateDevices() returns empty MediaDeviceInfo.label strings until a successful getUserMedia call grants permission. The camera-picker pattern in Section 21.6 accommodates this with the two-stage "Detect cameras" call-to-action.
  • WebRTC over self-signed origins works on every browser in the matrix after the user clicks through the cert warning. window.isSecureContext evaluates to true once the page loads over HTTPS, regardless of cert-validation outcome (per the Web Hypertext Application Technology Working Group Secure Contexts specification: the algorithm checks the URL scheme, not the cert validation status).

23. Prompt Builder User Interface #

23.1 The 7 canonical LocateAnything-3B prompt templates (verbatim from worker/prompts.py)

Verify against the file /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/worker/prompts.py lines 18-21 and 62-80 at implementation time. This asymmetry is intentional in the model's training data.

23.2 Per-template hardcoded generation_mode

The generation_mode parameter is not exposed as a user-facing dropdown. It is hardcoded per template based on the F1-score deltas reported in /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/docs/MODEL_CAPABILITIES.md:87-125:

TemplateHardcoded generation_modeRationale
detectionhybridDefault balanced mode; F1 within 1 point of slow for most detection tasks.
phrase_singlehybridSame.
phrase_multihybridSame.
text_groundingslowLargest mode-delta in the benchmark: F1 gain of up to +25 points on Scanned Receipts OCR and Information Extraction (SROIE) compared to fast.
scene_textslowSame OCR-domain reasoning.
gui_boxhybridDefault.
pointslowHeadline drone-demo case: VisDrone F1 +1.0 at slow versus hybrid.

The user-friendly card displays a small subtitle "(uses slow mode)" on the affected three cards (text_grounding, scene_text, point) so the user understands the latency difference. No dropdown, no choice — sovereign and opinionated.

23.3 Entry user-interface flow — viewport-fitting compact grid

  1. User claims the streamer slot via "Claim Streamer" button (the Lobby macro-state CTA from Section 21.0.14).
  2. Server replies ClaimResult::Granted; the WebAssembly client transitions the macro-state to PromptBuilder.
  3. Display: a 7-card grid sized to fill the 1fr stage row of the root grid (Section 21.0.2) — the page never scrolls. The grid uses repeat(auto-fit, minmax(180px, 1fr)) + grid-auto-rows: 1fr so every card is the same size and the column count adapts to viewport width via pure CSS, no JavaScript and no orientation media-query branching needed.
  4. Each card shows: an icon glyph, a bold human-friendly card title (from Section 23.1), and a one-line subtitle (e.g., "Find one specific thing", "Locate all categories matching", "Reads visible text"). On the worst-case viewport (Apple iPhone SE landscape at 568 × 320 CSS pixels, where the stage is ~200 CSS pixels tall) the subtitle is collapsed via the media-query rule below and only icon + title show.
  5. Tap a card → swap the macro-substate to PromptBuilder::Form(template); the grid unmounts via <Show when=...> and the per-template form mounts in its place. A "Back" pill appears in <footer class="hud-bottom"> alongside the "Submit" pill (initially disabled until validation passes per Section 23.6).

Worst-case viewport verification (the cell calculations confirm 7 cards fit without scroll on every device in the Section 22.1 matrix):

  • Apple iPhone SE portrait 320 × 568, stage ≈ 448 CSS pixels tall after safe-area + footer. Grid: 1 column × 7 rows, each ~64 px tall. The subtitle is collapsed below the height threshold.
  • Apple iPhone SE landscape 568 × 320, stage ≈ 200 CSS pixels tall. Grid: 3 columns (568/180 = 3.15 → 3) × 3 rows = 9 cells (7 filled, 2 empty). Each cell ~189 × 66 px — fits the touch-target floor, subtitle collapsed.
  • Samsung Galaxy S25 portrait 360 × 800, stage ≈ 680 px. Grid: 2 × 4 = 8 cells (7 filled, 1 empty). Each cell ~180 × 170 px — comfortable.
  • Apple iPad Pro 11-inch portrait 834 × 1194, stage ≈ 1074 px. Grid: 4 × 2 = 8 cells. Each cell ~209 × 537 px — spacious.
  • Desktop 1280 × 720 minimum, stage ≈ 600 px. Grid: 7 × 1 = 7 cells, each ~183 × 600 px — single-row, generous.

The card markup and per-component Cascading Style Sheets rules (extending the canonical skeleton of Section 21.0.15):

<button class="prompt-card" type="button" on:click=move |_| pick_template(t)>
    <span class="prompt-card-icon" aria-hidden="true">{icon_glyph(t)}</span>
    <span class="prompt-card-title">{title(t)}</span>
    <span class="prompt-card-subtitle">{subtitle(t)}</span>
</button>
/* Appended to wasm-client/styles.css after the canonical 21.0.15 skeleton. */
.prompt-grid {
    display: grid;
    grid-template-columns: repeat(auto-fit, minmax(180px, 1fr));
    grid-auto-rows: 1fr;
    gap: var(--gap-lg);
    padding: var(--gap-lg);
    height: 100%;
    width: 100%;
}
.prompt-card {
    display: grid;
    grid-template-columns: auto 1fr;
    grid-template-rows: auto auto;
    gap: 4px 8px;
    padding: var(--gap-lg);
    min-height: var(--touch-min);
    background: var(--bg-elev);
    border: 1px solid var(--border);
    border-radius: var(--radius);
    color: var(--fg);
    text-align: left;
    cursor: pointer;
    font: inherit;
}
.prompt-card-icon     { grid-row: 1 / span 2; align-self: center; font-size: 24px; }
.prompt-card-title    { font-weight: 600; }
.prompt-card-subtitle { color: var(--fg-muted); font-size: 13px; }
/* Collapse the subtitle on cramped cells (iPhone SE landscape, ~66 px rows). */
@media (max-height: 600px) and (orientation: landscape) {
    .prompt-card { padding: var(--gap); }
    .prompt-card-subtitle { display: none; }
}

The icon glyph is a CSS-rendered shape (one of seven inline SVG paths, served from styles.css via background-image: url("data:image/svg+xml,...") so the img-src directive is not invoked). The three cards with hardcoded generation_mode: slow (text_grounding, scene_text, point per Section 23.2) carry a small "(slow mode)" suffix in the subtitle; under the height-collapse media query the suffix is also hidden.

The per-template form (Section 23.4 below) and the live-preview pane (Section 23.5) live inside the stage in either side-by-side (landscape) or stacked (portrait) layout via the orientation media queries from Section 21.0.4; the form column is the .form-scroll sanctioned inner-scroll region.

23.4 Per-template form controls

detection
N rows of <input type="text">, one per category. "Add category" button below (cap at 10 categories). Per-row "Remove" button (X) hidden when only one row remains. The WebAssembly client joins values with literal </c> separator (no whitespace) when constructing the final prompt. The user never types </c> directly.
phrase_single
One <input type="text"> with placeholder "e.g. the red drone closest to the camera".
phrase_multi
One <input type="text"> with placeholder "e.g. drones in the sky". Single field, not multi-row — template 3 takes one free-form phrase, not a </c>-list.
text_grounding
One <input type="text"> labeled "Text to find:" with placeholder "STOP".
scene_text
No user input. Submit button enabled immediately; the preview pane shows the verbatim canonical prompt string.
gui_box
One <input type="text"> labeled "UI element:" with placeholder "the search button".
point
One <input type="text"> labeled "Point at:" with placeholder "drone in the sky".

Every input field has these attributes: maxlength="200", live character counter, autocapitalize="off", autocorrect="off", spellcheck="false", inputmode="text".

23.5 Live preview pane

Always rendered below the form. Use a <pre> element with class preview, styled via the external styles.css with white-space: pre-wrap; font-family: ui-monospace;. Label: "Final prompt sent to LocateAnything:". Updates on every keystroke via Leptos reactive signals. This is the single most important affordance: the user sees the exact bytes LocateAnything-3B will receive, no template hiding.

23.6 Frontend validation rules (strict subset of LA's prompt_validator.rs)

On every input change, the WebAssembly client runs the following checks. Every check is "show inline error and disable Submit". No "strip-and-warn", no silent mutation of user input. The user fixes their input; the system never invisibly rewrites it.

  1. Leading or trailing whitespace: if raw != raw.trim(), show inline error "remove leading/trailing whitespace" and disable Submit. Do not silently trim. The preview pane displays exactly raw so the user sees what they typed.
  2. Non-empty: if raw.is_empty() AND the template requires a slot, disable Submit (no error text; an empty required field is self-evident).
  3. Length cap: if raw.chars().count() > 200, show inline error "too long (max 200 characters)" and disable Submit. (Well under LocateAnything-3B's whole-prompt cap of MAX_PROMPT_CHARS = 16384; the demo deliberately enforces a tighter cap to match the prompt-builder user-interface idiom.)
  4. No control characters: if raw.chars().any(|c| c.is_control()), show inline error "control characters not allowed".
  5. No manual </c> or angle-bracket fragments: if raw.contains("</c>") OR raw.contains("</") OR raw.contains("c>"), show inline error "do not type angle-bracket fragments directly; use Add Category for multiple targets". The broader check catches partial-fragment inputs like "foo</c" or "c>bar" that would otherwise pass the literal-4-char check and then concatenate ambiguously with the literal </c> separator during prompt assembly. (LocateAnything-3B's server-side prompt_validator.rs is the ultimate authoritative validator and rejects malformed prompts via the type:"error" reply path that Section 23.9 handles — this client-side rule is defense-in-depth, not the full guarantee.)
  6. Point slot — no comma: if the active template is point and raw.contains(','), show inline error "single category only; no commas".
  7. Detection row — no comma: same for each detection row.
  8. No trailing period in user input: if raw.ends_with('.'), show inline error "remove the trailing period; the canonical template adds it for you". Disable Submit. Do not silently strip. The user removes the period; the system never invisibly mutates input.
  9. Unicode normalization form: if raw is not in Normalization Form Canonical Composition (NFC), show inline error "this text contains a non-NFC Unicode form; please retype the input". The check is raw.chars().eq(raw.nfc()) via the unicode-normalization crate version =0.1.25 compiled into the WebAssembly bundle. Requires use unicode_normalization::UnicodeNormalization; in scope (the trait that adds the .nfc() method to &str and to any Iterator<Item = char>; verified at /tmp/unicode-norm-src/src/lib.rs:99-110, 133, 197). Disable Submit. Do not silently normalize.

The Submit button is disabled (visually muted) until every rule passes for every visible slot.

Why no silent mutation: the user's stated principle is "extremely strict server-side input validation" and "no fallbacks". Silently trimming whitespace or stripping trailing periods is exactly the silently-more-lenient pattern that hides bugs and confuses users when they later observe that LocateAnything-3B received a string that differs from what they typed. The strict rule is: the bytes the LocateAnything-3B server sees are the bytes the user typed inside the slot, surrounded by the canonical-template prefix and the canonical trailing period (or no trailing period for templates that don't require it). Any deviation is the user's responsibility to fix in the input field.

23.7 Unicode normalization is rejected, not applied

Previous draft of this plan considered applying Normalization Form Canonical Composition (NFC) at submit time, with a footnote "silently more lenient than LocateAnything-3B; honest gap". That has been removed. The strict-correctness behavior is rule 9 of Section 23.6: detect non-NFC input and refuse the submission with an inline error. The WebAssembly client never silently normalizes; the user retypes.

The unicode-normalization crate version =0.1.25 is added to the WebAssembly client's Cargo.toml for the comparison check only; the crate's nfc() iterator is consumed only inside the equality predicate, never used to mutate the input string.

Section 7.5's pin table is updated to include unicode-normalization = "=0.1.25", default-features = false as a WebAssembly client dependency.

23.8 Atomic claim message

Submit sends SignalMessage::Claim(ClaimMsg { prompt, generation_mode }) with both fields populated atomically. No separate set_prompt message. Why atomic: bundling avoids a race window where the streamer is Claimed but has no prompt. The prompt is locked for the entire ownership session. To change the prompt, the user releases ownership and re-claims.

23.9 LA error flow

If LocateAnything-3B returns {"type":"error","frame_id":...,"code":"...","message":"..."} for a frame, the demo server propagates it back to the streamer as SignalMessage::Error with code: "prompt_rejected". The WebAssembly client renders the error as a banner ("LocateAnything rejected the prompt: "), then schedules automatic ownership release after 500 milliseconds, then transitions the user-interface state back to the 7-card prompt-builder grid.

24. Scripts and Operator Setup #

Mirrors the discipline of /home/user/Desktop/locate_anything_setup/scripts/:

24.1 website/scripts/00_validate_host.sh

Preflight check. Verifies (no network operations):

  • Docker installed and the user is in the docker group (test with docker ps succeeding).
  • TCP port 8443 is currently free on the host.
  • UDP port 51000 is currently free on the host.
  • Free disk space at the project directory >= 5 gibibytes (the Docker image is approximately 600 mebibytes; the bind volume needs space for cert files only).
  • Not running as root.
  • Architecture invariant — uname -m returns x86_64. The project's Docker base image is built for linux/amd64; running on aarch64, armv7l, etc. requires either rebuilding the image for the target arch or running under QEMU emulation, neither of which is supported by the committed build pipeline.
  • Docker daemon reachable — docker info >/dev/null 2>&1 succeeds. Fail-loud message identifies the two common causes: the docker.service systemd unit is not running, OR the operator is not in the docker group.
  • Docker server version ≥ 24.x — parses docker version --format '{{.Server.Version}}' and asserts the major number is at least 24. Older Docker engines lack the BuildKit features the multi-stage Dockerfile relies on (cache mounts with sharing=locked, --network=none on RUN steps, the BuildKit-1.7 syntax directive).
  • .gitignore contains .runtime/ — invariant-checked via grep -Eq '(^|/)\.runtime/?($|$)' "${PROJECT_DIR}/.gitignore" (or equivalent). A stray git add of the operator's secrets is catastrophic; this discipline cannot rely on operator memory.

Concrete shapes (for the implementation agent — fail-loud chained shell errors throughout):

# (1) Architecture.
arch=$(uname -m)
if [[ "$arch" != "x86_64" ]]; then
    die "uname -m reports \"$arch\"; this project's Docker base image is \
linux/amd64. Running on aarch64 etc. requires either rebuilding the image \
for the target arch or running under QEMU emulation, neither of which is \
supported by the committed build pipeline."
fi

# (2) Docker daemon reachable.
if ! docker info >/dev/null 2>&1; then
    die "Docker daemon not reachable; check that the docker.service systemd \
unit is running and the operator is in the \`docker\` group \
(\`sudo systemctl status docker\` and \`groups | grep -w docker\`)"
fi

# (3) Docker server version ≥ 24.x.
docker_server_version=$(docker version --format '{{.Server.Version}}')
docker_major=${docker_server_version%%.*}
if (( docker_major < 24 )); then
    die "Docker server version $docker_server_version is too old; require ≥ 24.x \
for the BuildKit features used by the multi-stage Dockerfile (cache mounts \
with sharing=locked, --network=none on RUN steps, the 1.7 syntax directive)"
fi

# (4) .gitignore contains .runtime/.
if ! grep -Eq '(^|/)\.runtime/?($|$)' "${PROJECT_DIR}/.gitignore"; then
    die "${PROJECT_DIR}/.gitignore must contain a .runtime/ entry; a stray \
\`git add\` of .runtime/config.env or .runtime/state/ would commit the \
operator's auth secret AND the private TLS key. This invariant is checked \
on every run."
fi

Fails loud on any check failure with an explicit message naming the offending precondition.

24.2 website/scripts/01_build_image.sh

Reads DOCKER_BUILDER_DIGEST and DOCKER_RUNTIME_DIGEST from scripts/lib/versions.sh (the committed maintainer-set values per Section 7.2) and passes them to docker build via --build-arg LA_BUILDER_DIGEST=${DOCKER_BUILDER_DIGEST} --build-arg LA_RUNTIME_DIGEST=${DOCKER_RUNTIME_DIGEST}, along with --build-arg LA_WEBSITE_GIT_SHA=$(git rev-parse HEAD) and --build-arg LA_WEBSITE_BUILD_TIME_UTC=$(date -u +%FT%TZ). The full docker build invocation is the one in Section 15.7.9 (with --pull=false to prevent silent digest drift).

The script does NOT docker pull the floating tag and does NOT mutate versions.sh (Section 7.2's policy correction). Digest capture is the project maintainer's release-time procedure, committed once per base-image bump; operators consume the committed values. If the digest in versions.sh doesn't match a digest available on Docker Hub at build time (e.g., the maintainer used a digest from a since-pruned mirror), docker build fails loud — that is the desired behavior, not a fallback to re-capture.

24.3 website/scripts/02_start_service.sh

The container start script. Reads operator choices from the project-local .runtime/config.env (written by setup.sh, Section 24.7), sources project-internal constants from scripts/lib/versions.sh, and runs docker run with all paths and identity bound to the operator's UID. No operator-specific value lives in any committed script.

The script's full preamble:

#!/usr/bin/env bash
# website/scripts/02_start_service.sh — start the la-website container.
set -Eeuo pipefail

_SCRIPT_DIR="$( cd "$( dirname "${BASH_SOURCE[0]}" )" && pwd )"
source "${_SCRIPT_DIR}/lib/common.sh"
load_versions          # populates LA_WEBSITE_IMAGE_TAG from versions.sh

# Project paths (computed from script location). The website project lives
# in the operator's home directory; nothing here touches /etc or /var.
readonly PROJECT_DIR="$( cd "${_SCRIPT_DIR}/.." && pwd )"
readonly RUNTIME_DIR="${PROJECT_DIR}/.runtime"
readonly STATE_DIR_HOST="${RUNTIME_DIR}/state"
readonly CONFIG_PATH="${RUNTIME_DIR}/config.env"

# === Concurrent-run guard (docker-name uniqueness) =========================
