Verify: trunk build --release (run from the workspace root so Trunk.toml's [tools] pins apply — never cd wasm-client, §15.4) succeeds; the resulting wasm-client/dist/index.html contains a single <script type="module"> block (sanity check for the CSP hash injection).
  11. End-to-end on host (no Docker yet). Run the server binary on the host, open https://127.0.0.1:8443/#supersecrettoken123 in Apple Safari and Google Chrome desktop, click through the cert warning, verify the streamer claim flow works, verify viewer fan-out works, verify bounding-box overlays render in both roles.
  12. Dockerfile. Write the multi-stage Dockerfile per Section 15.5. Write website/scripts/01_build_image.sh. Verify: bash scripts/01_build_image.sh produces a runnable image; docker run la-website:<version> --help prints clap help text.
  13. Operator scripts. Write website/scripts/00_validate_host.sh, website/scripts/02_start_service.sh, website/scripts/03_smoke_test.sh, website/setup.sh, website/uninstall.sh. Verify: the full bash setup.sh orchestration completes cleanly.
  14. End-to-end in Docker on localhost. Run bash setup.sh; smoke test passes; manually verify the demo works in a browser at https://127.0.0.1:8443/#<token>.
  15. Operator-facing README. Write website/README.md covering: host prerequisites; how to set --auth-secret securely; how to interpret the cert warning; the manual cert-regeneration procedure every ~27 months; the --bind-all-interfaces flag and its security implications; the iOS cert-trust workflow; troubleshooting common failures.
  16. Honest shortcut report. Document every shortcut, every untested branch, every defensive-correctness concession, every honest gap left unresolved. Submit to the operator (the user) for review.
  17. Approval gate. Wait for the operator's explicit approval before any --bind-all-interfaces deployment.

26. Explicitly Deferred Decisions #

These were considered and deferred deliberately, with the rationale recorded so a future revisit has context.

Traversal Using Relays around Network Address Translation (TURN) server
Not deployed initially. The metric for adding TURN: rate of IceConnectionStateChange::Disconnected within 30 seconds of peer admission exceeds 2 percent sustained over two consecutive rolling windows of 100 admitted peers (collected via the tracing log surface). On meeting that metric: deploy coturn in a sidecar container (sovereign — we run it).
WebSocket protocol version field
Skipped. Both halves of the workspace ship from the same git commit; version skew between connected peers is impossible by construction. Easy to add later via #[serde(default)] on a protocol_version: u32 field of the Claim message.
'unsafe-hashes' Content Security Policy directive for inline style attributes
Rejected. 'unsafe-hashes' would let us hash-pin style="..." attributes, but it permits ANY hashed value to appear in ANY attribute — a class-wide weakening. We use external Cascading Style Sheets discipline (Section 16) instead, achieving full style-src 'self' tightness.
Binaryen wasm-opt version newer than 116
The Rust crate wasm-opt 0.116.1 pins Binaryen at version 116 (released March 2024). Upstream Binaryen is at version 129 (released April 2026). The newer optimizer would catch a few more optimization opportunities but the crates.io-only path is sovereign; the alternative is a CMake-from-source build adding a one-time git clone of WebAssembly/binaryen. Reconsider only if a specific newer Binaryen feature is needed.
Public IPv4 rotation after long outage resolved
Not a concern for this deployment. The host machine at /home/user/Desktop/personal_server/ has a static public IPv4 address provided by the Internet Service Provider and a corresponding Domain Name System record. The address does not rotate; no mitigation needed. If a future deployment had a dynamic-IP residential connection, the operator should pass a Domain Name System hostname (not an Internet Protocol literal) to --public-host, and the cert's Subject Alternative Name list would include the hostname plus the resolved address at startup — when the address changes after a restart, the cert is regenerated automatically by Section 14.5's "SAN set mismatch" branch.
Apple iOS Configuration Profile (.mobileconfig) trust workflow
Documented in the user-facing ?help=ios-cert subpage for power users who want persistent cert trust on Apple iOS. The basic flow uses click-through-per-session.
Trunk data-inline inline-style behavior
Banned by convention (continuous-integration grep check rejects any data-inline attribute on Cascading Style Sheets <link> tags in wasm-client/index.html).

27. Honest Gaps from Research #

These are the items that genuinely could not be resolved from cloned source and require empirical verification or operational experience.

  • mozjpeg encode latency at 720p on the target host. Estimated 8 to 15 milliseconds based on extrapolation from libjpeg-turbo benchmarks. Run a microbenchmark in continuous-integration on the target box to confirm. If the actual number exceeds 30 milliseconds, reconsider the quality setting — at that point mozjpeg starts to be a meaningful fraction of LocateAnything-3B's fastest mode (point_to at ~210 ms), and a non-trivial fraction of any plausibly-faster successor model.
  • DataChannel "bye" flush budget (~800 ms) at shutdown / drain. The reference chat.rs uses no drain; the ~800 ms per-shutdown bye-flush cap (§18.2 step 3) is our defensive choice. The DataChannel "bye" payload plus the SCTP shutdown chunk may not have flushed within ~800 ms under heavy congestion. (This is the bye-FLUSH budget, distinct from the FSM Draining→Idle window — which is DRAIN_TIMEOUT = 30 s for an unintentional drop, or the same ~800 ms fast bye-flush for an intentional release; see §11.1/§11.2.) Empirical observation will tell.
  • Apple iOS 26-specific behavior. No Apple release notes documenting changes to the 825-day cert cap, click-through persistence, or WebRTC behavior versus iOS 17-18 baseline. Assumed continuous. Verify on a real Apple iPhone 17 device when one is available.
  • Per-viewer SCTP pacing under N=100 viewer load. str0m's single-thread model may bottleneck before SCTP send buffers fill. Untested at scale. The expected demo audience is small (single-digit to low-double-digit viewers), so this is unlikely to bite in practice.
  • The exact 720p mozjpeg-baseline encode latency on the target Docker container's specific CPU model. Order-of-magnitude bound only; could be plus or minus 2-times.
  • Browser-side ICE-disconnected timeout after our Rtc::disconnect(). Approximately 5 seconds per RFC 7675 baseline, but implementations vary; could be up to 30 seconds. Not load-bearing for our flow (we send DataChannel "bye" before disconnecting, so the user sees a clean handoff).
  • NFC tokenizer behavior on accepted input. The WebAssembly client now REJECTS non-NFC input (Section 23.6 rule 9), so this gap is mostly closed. Residual gap: LocateAnything-3B's tokenizer behavior on NFC-but-degenerate-Unicode (combining marks, ZWJ sequences, regional-indicator pairs) is not separately validated by the demo. If a user types NFC text that the tokenizer mishandles, the model may behave inconsistently. Operationally: rare; operator-discoverable.

28. Approval Gate Before --bind-all-interfaces #

Per the user's stated requirement: "The default launch should launch the docker image such that the only port we listen on is on 127.0.0.1, then just as with the locate_anything_setup server project, there should be a flag that needs to be set to set up the server in such a way as to listen on 0.0.0.0. You'll only get to expose on 0.0.0.0 after I fully approve the correctness of your implementation."

Therefore:

  1. The default container start binds 127.0.0.1:8443 (HTTPS+WSS) and 127.0.0.1:51000 (UDP for WebRTC and own-STUN). No external reachability.
  2. End-to-end testing happens on 127.0.0.1 only.
  3. After implementation is complete, the implementation agent writes the honest shortcut report (Section 25, step 16).
  4. The user reviews the implementation and the report.
  5. The user explicitly approves the --bind-all-interfaces deployment.
  6. Only then: re-run the host network-security audit script at /home/user/Desktop/personal_server/network_security/verify_network_security.py to verify the new externally-reachable ports (8443 TCP and 51000 UDP) are appropriate to the host's overall security posture.
  7. Only after that audit passes: start the container with --bind-all-interfaces.

The implementation agent must not enable --bind-all-interfaces autonomously. This is the user's gate, not the implementation agent's call.

Appendix A — Quick Reference: Critical "Do Not Forget" Items #

  1. Use KeyframeRequestKind::Pli, NOT Fir. The str0m chat.rs example is wrong per RFC 5104.
  2. Force H.264 on both sides. Server: str0m::Rtc::builder().clear_codecs().enable_h264(true).... Client (WebAssembly): RtcRtpTransceiver::set_codec_preferences() with H.264 profile-level-id=42e01f packetization-mode=1 only, before createOffer(). WITHOUT this, default str0m + default Chrome negotiate VP8 (str0m's codec_config.rs:65-76 default order is VP8-first; sdp.rs:1483-1498 emits answer in local order, not offerer order). Apple Safari prefers 640c1f (Constrained High); client-side filter forces 42e01f.
  3. Call compress.set_optimize_scans(false) on every mozjpeg Compress. The default is the 45-times-slower path.
  4. The Leptos crate version is =0.8.19. Version 0.8.18 never existed on crates.io (verified 2026-06-01 via crates.io API). Earlier drafts of this plan had this inverted as "0.8.19 doesn't exist; use 0.8.18" — that was a propagated error from an earlier research summary. The correct pin is =0.8.19.
  5. ffmpeg-next is version 7.1.0, not 8.1.0. Debian Trixie ships FFmpeg 7.1.4.
  6. Hand-write extern declarations for HtmlVideoElement::requestVideoFrameCallback and the playsinline attribute setter. web-sys 0.3.99 does not bind them.
  7. The cert validity period is 824 days, not 100 years. Apple Security framework caps at 825.
  8. Bounding-box wire format is normalized [0.0, 1.0] floating-point. Server converts from LocateAnything-3B's [0, 1000] integer grid by dividing by 1000.
  9. Trunk's offline behavior: pre-install wasm-bindgen-cli 0.2.122 and wasm-opt 0.116.1 via cargo install --locked --version ... AND set TRUNK_OFFLINE=true AND pass --offline. Otherwise Trunk fetches from GitHub at build time.
  10. Single Command-Line Interface argument --public-host drives the TLS SAN, WebRTC host candidate, and browser STUN URL. NO separate --public-ip.
  11. The demo server runs its own STUN server on the same UDP port as WebRTC. NO third-party STUN.
  12. IPv4-only binding, both modes. Default 127.0.0.1, opt-in 0.0.0.0. No IPv6 socket is ever opened; the cert SAN list excludes IPv6; the smoke test does not probe an IPv6 listener. --public-host resolving to an IPv6 address causes the binary to refuse to start.
  13. The SPA bundle (/, fingerprinted JS/WASM/CSS) is served WITHOUT auth — the first browser GET cannot carry an Authorization header because the URL fragment is client-side per RFC 3986. The auth-gated surface is the API: /v1/info, /v1/capabilities, /v1/signal.
  14. No HSTS header. Would brick the click-through path on cert regen.
  15. No 'unsafe-inline' in style-src. Use external Cascading Style Sheets and style:NAME=VALUE Leptos directives (which use setProperty and are exempt from CSP style-src).
  16. str0m::Rtc::disconnect only sets self.alive = false. Send a DataChannel "bye" and pump poll_output BEFORE calling it.
  17. ICE consent freshness in str0m is approximately 21.5 seconds, NOT RFC 7675's nominal 30 seconds.
  18. str0m 0.20 has no IceConnectionState::Failed variant. Watch Disconnected instead.
  19. All error handling is anyhow-style chained strings. No unwrap(), no expect(), no panic!() in runtime code.
  20. The implementation agent can and should spawn its own research sub-agents (Agent tool with subagent_type: "general-purpose") to clone pinned versions into /tmp for source-level verification when any detail is unclear.
